  fails: the genus-$g$ free energy receives a cross-channel
  correction $\delta F_g^{\mathrm{cross}}$
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:multi-weight-genus-expansion}).
  Test~2 holds at genus~$1$; at genus~$\geq 2$ the scalar
  formula is replaced by the multi-weight decomposition
  (Open Problem~\ref{op:multi-generator-universality}, resolved
  negatively).
\item \emph{BV/BRST $=$ bar at higher genus.}
  For the Heisenberg, the scalar-level identification
  $F_g^{\mathrm{BV}} = F_g^{\mathrm{bar}} = \kappa\cdot\lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$
  is proved at all genera
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:heisenberg-bv-bar-all-genera}).
  The general chain-level identification at genus $g \geq 1$
  is conjectural
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:master-bv-brst}).  Tests~1--4 control
  the bar side; the BV/BRST comparison is an independent
  assertion about the physics.
\item \emph{Non-perturbative completion.}
  The four tests are perturbative in genus.  The
  algebraic shadow obstruction tower $\sum_g F_g \hbar^{2g}$ converges
  when the shadow radius $\rho(\cA) < 1$; for
  $\rho \geq 1$ (Virasoro at $c < c^* \approx 6.125$), the
  series is a formal asymptotic expansion.  The comparison
  between the algebraic tower and the analytic sewing envelope
  $\cA^{\mathrm{sew}}$ is
  Conjecture~\ref{conj:analytic-realization}.
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}

% ============================================================
\subsection{The four-test boundary of control}
\label{subsec:concordance-four-test-boundary}
\index{boundary of control|textbf}
\index{four-test boundary|textbf}

The algebraic engine controls everything
\emph{inside} the modular Koszul locus.  The boundary
of that locus is determined by four independent tests,
each representing a genuine mathematical barrier that the
engine does not cross.

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{DK-3 categorical test.}
  The factorization Koszul duality functor
  $\Phi \colon \operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}
  (\cA) \xrightarrow{\sim}
  \operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}
  (\cA^!)^{\mathrm{op}}$
  is proved on the evaluation-generated core at all simple
  types
  (Corollary~\ref{cor:dk23-all-types}).
  Extension beyond this core to the full module category
  requires categorical input (pro-nilpotent completion,
  prefundamental modules, thick generation beyond evaluation
  objects) that is not derivable from the MC element alone.
  The engine produces the $r$-matrix; it does not produce
  the full quantum group.

\item \textbf{Lattice-only arithmetic test.}
  The Hecke--Newton closure
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:hecke-newton-lattice}) and the
  unconditional Ramanujan corollary
  (Corollary~\ref{cor:unconditional-lattice}) are proved
  for lattice VOAs, where the shadow amplitudes are chiral
  graph integrals that factor through Satake parameters.
  For non-lattice algebras, the arithmetic of the OPE is
  not controlled: the MC equation provides moment
  $L$-functions, but prime-locality transfer from
  $\mathrm{GL}(2)$ to $\mathrm{GL}(r+1)$ for $r \geq 5$
  is open
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:modular-spectral-rigidity}).
  The engine computes all symmetric-power moments; it does
  not prove their automorphy.

\item \textbf{Chirally Koszul geometric test.}
  Every theorem in the engine assumes chiral Koszulness
  (Definition~\ref{def:chiral-koszul-morphism}):
  $H^n(\barBch(\cA), d) = 0$ for $n \geq 3$.
  The PBW criterion
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:pbw-koszulness-criterion}) proves this
  for all freely strongly generated algebras.
  For simple quotients at admissible levels, the PBW
  filtration may degenerate, and Koszulness is open
  (\S\ref{subsec:concordance-true-frontier}, item~1).
  The engine works inside the Koszul world; it does not
  detect whether an algebra is Koszul.

\item \textbf{Shadow radius $\rho < 1$ analytic test.}
  The shadow obstruction tower converges absolutely when the shadow
  growth rate $\rho(\cA) < 1$
  (Definition~\ref{def:shadow-growth-rate};
  Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-radius}).
  For $\rho \geq 1$, the tower is a formal asymptotic
  expansion (Borel summable by
  Proposition~\ref{prop:carleman-virasoro},
  but not absolutely convergent).
  The engine computes shadow coefficients at every finite
  arity; it does not sum the series when $\rho \geq 1$.
  The sewing envelope $\cA^{\mathrm{sew}}$
  (Hausdorff completion for sewing-amplitude seminorms)
  replaces formal summation with analytic convergence, but
  the comparison between the algebraic shadow obstruction tower and the
  analytic sewing envelope is itself an open problem
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:analytic-realization}).
\end{enumerate}

\noindent
Each test is necessary and independent: an algebra can pass
three tests and fail the fourth.  The Virasoro algebra at
generic~$c$ passes tests~1--3 but has $\rho(\mathrm{Vir}_c)
> 1$ for $c < c^* \approx 6.125$.
The simple quotient $L_k(\fg)$ at an admissible level may
fail test~3 while passing the others.
Lattice VOAs pass all four tests; they are the algebras for
which the engine achieves maximal reach.

\subsection{Two orthogonal axes}
\label{subsec:concordance-two-orthogonal-axes}
\index{critical level!orthogonal axis|textbf}
\index{shadow tower!orthogonal to critical level|textbf}

The algebraic engine operates on two regimes that are
mathematically orthogonal.  The point of separation is the
modular characteristic $\kappa(\cA)$.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Axis~1: Critical-level bar cohomology
($\kappa = 0$).}\enspace
At the critical level $k = -h^\vee$, the curvature $\kappa$
vanishes and the bar complex is uncurved: $d^2 = 0$ on
$\barBch(\widehat{\fg}_{-h^\vee})$.  The mathematical content
lies in bar \emph{cohomology}:
\[
  H^0(\barBch(\widehat{\fg}_{-h^\vee}))
  \;\cong\;
  \operatorname{Fun}(\operatorname{Op}_{\fg^\vee}(D))
\]
recovers the Feigin--Frenkel center
(Theorem~\ref{thm:oper-bar-h0-dl}), and the full
cohomological package
$H^n(\barBch(\widehat{\fg}_{-h^\vee})) \cong
\Omega^n(\operatorname{Op}_{\fg^\vee}(D))$
recovers the oper differential-form package
(Theorem~\ref{thm:oper-bar}).
The relevant tools are homological algebra on the bar
complex (Ext groups, spectral sequences, derived categories),
and the target objects are opers, the geometric Langlands
correspondence, and the center of the completed
enveloping algebra at critical level.

The shadow obstruction tower is trivial on this axis: since $\kappa = 0$,
Theorem~D gives $\mathrm{obs}_g = 0$ for all $g \geq 1$, and
for the commutative critical-level algebra the full MC element
$\Theta_\cA = 0$ (the OPE structure constants vanish; see
Remark~\ref{rem:dk-shadow-status}).
The shadow obstruction tower,
the discriminant, the four-class partition G/L/C/M, and the
genus expansion are all inert.  The information is in the
kernel of the bar differential, not in its cokernel.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Axis~2: Off-critical shadow obstruction tower ($\kappa \neq 0$).}\enspace
Away from the critical level, $\kappa \neq 0$ and the bar
complex is curved: $d_1^2 = [\kappa \cdot \omega_g, -]$.
The MC element $\Theta_\cA \neq 0$ and the shadow obstruction
tower is nontrivial.  The mathematical content lies in
\emph{deformation theory}: the modular characteristic
$\kappa$, the cubic shadow~$C$, the quartic
resonance class~$Q$, the discriminant~$\Delta$, the growth
rate~$\rho$, the four-class partition, the genus expansion,
and all five main theorems.

The relevant tools are Maurer--Cartan theory in the modular
convolution algebra, graph sums on stable curves, and
the shadow connection $\nabla^{\mathrm{sh}}$.  The target
objects are tautological classes on $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$,
free-energy asymptotics, and CohFT structure.

On this axis, bar cohomology is \emph{not} the primary object:
the bar complex is curved, so $d^2 \neq 0$ and ordinary
cohomology is undefined.  The correct replacement is the
MC moduli space $\MC(\gAmod)$ and its projections.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Orthogonality.}\enspace
These two axes meet only at the degenerate point
$\kappa = 0$, $\Theta_\cA = 0$, $H^*(\barBch) = \text{oper
package}$.  No theorem on axis~1 implies a theorem on
axis~2, and conversely.  The Feigin--Frenkel involution
$k \mapsto -k - 2h^\vee$ maps $\kappa \mapsto -\kappa$ and
therefore exchanges the two sides of axis~2 (the algebra and
its Koszul dual), but it does not connect axis~2 to axis~1.
The critical level is a fixed point of the involution
($k = -h^\vee$ maps to itself), confirming that axis~1 is
invariant and isolated.

The monograph develops both axes: the oper package of
Chapter~\ref{chap:kac-moody} and the critical-level
Hochschild computation of
Theorem~\ref{thm:critical-level-cohomology} belong to
axis~1; the shadow obstruction tower, the genus expansion, and
Theorems~A--D belong to axis~2.
Theorem~H (chiral Hochschild) connects them: the polynomial
ring $\mathbb{C}[\Theta_1, \ldots, \Theta_r]$ at generic
level degenerates to the exterior$\otimes$polynomial ring
$\Lambda^*(P_1, \ldots, P_r) \otimes
\mathbb{C}[\Theta_1, \ldots, \Theta_r]$ at critical level.

\begin{conjecture}[Isomonodromic shadow deformation; \ClaimStatusConjectured]%
\label{conj:isomonodromic-shadow}%
\index{isomonodromic deformation!shadow tower}%
\index{shadow tower!isomonodromic deformation}%
\index{Gaudin Hamiltonian!shadow tower}%
\index{KZ connection!isomonodromic deformation}%
As the level~$k$ moves from the critical value~$-h^\vee$ to
generic values, the oper eigenvalues of the Gaudin Hamiltonian
deform continuously into the shadow obstruction tower curvature data
$(\kappa, \alpha, S_4)$.  The deformation is isomonodromic:
the monodromy representation of the KZ connection is
preserved, while the Stokes data of the irregular singularity
at infinity changes.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[The oper--shadow bridge]%
\label{rem:oper-shadow-bridge}%
Conjecture~\ref{conj:isomonodromic-shadow} proposes a
precise bridge between axis~1 and axis~2.  At the critical
level $k = -h^\vee$, the bar cohomology
$H^0(\barBch(\widehat{\fg}_{-h^\vee}))$ recovers the algebra
of functions on opers (the Feigin--Frenkel theorem).  Away
from the critical level, the bar complex is curved
($\kappa \neq 0$) and ordinary cohomology is undefined; the
mathematical content is captured by the MC element
$\Theta_\cA$ and its shadow obstruction tower projections
$(\kappa, \alpha, S_4, \ldots)$.

The conjecture asserts that the passage from opers to the
shadow obstruction tower is an isomonodromic deformation in the
Jimbo--Miwa--Ueno sense: as $k$ moves away from $-h^\vee$,
the positions of the Gaudin spectral data change continuously
into the curvature invariants of the shadow obstruction tower, while the
monodromy of the KZ connection (which is flat for all~$k$)
is preserved.  The Stokes phenomenon at the irregular
singularity at infinity (invisible at the critical level
where the connection is regular) encodes the higher-arity
shadow data $S_4, S_5, \ldots$ that emerge off-critical.
In particular, the shadow obstruction tower records the Taylor
coefficients of this deformation in the parameter
$k + h^\vee$.
\end{remark}

% ============================================================
\subsection{Three Langlands gaps}
\label{subsec:concordance-langlands-gaps}
\index{Langlands programme!structural gaps}

The spectral continuation programme
(\S\ref{subsec:concordance-spectral-continuation} below)
explores arithmetic consequences of the shadow obstruction tower.
Before entering that programme, we state three structural
gaps between the proved core of this monograph and any
Langlands-type statement.  These are not technical
difficulties awaiting a clever argument; they are
category-level separations between the objects this
monograph constructs and the objects the Langlands
programme requires.

\begin{remark}[Gap~A: bar-cobar vs scattering]%
\label{rem:langlands-gap-a}%
\index{Langlands programme!Gap A (bar-cobar vs scattering)}%
\index{twisting morphism!vs scattering amplitude}%
\ClaimStatusOpen{}
The bar-cobar adjunction (Theorem~A) produces
\emph{twisting morphisms}: algebraic maps
$\tau \colon \barBch(\cA) \to \cA$ controlling the
coupling between a chiral algebra and its Koszul dual.
The Langlands programme requires \emph{scattering
amplitudes}: analytic objects whose poles on the complex
$s$-plane encode $L$-function zeros.  These are different
types of mathematical objects.  The twisting morphism
$\tau$ is a chain-level algebraic datum defined over
$\Ran(X)$; a scattering amplitude is an analytic function
of a complex variable~$s$ arising from a Mellin transform
of an automorphic form.

The spectral continuation programme
(\S\ref{subsec:concordance-spectral-continuation})
constructs a bridge for lattice VOAs: the sewing
determinant $\det(1 - K_q)$ has a Mellin transform
that produces~$L$-functions.  This bridge has two
components: (i)~the sewing--shadow intertwining
(Theorem~\ref{thm:sewing-shadow-intertwining}), which
identifies the sewing determinant with a Chern--Weil
pairing of~$\Theta_\cA$, and (ii)~the Hecke module
structure on~$\gAmod[V_\Lambda]$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:spectral-continuation-bridge}), which
provides analytic continuation.  For non-lattice theories,
step~(ii) is not available: the shadow spectral measure
and the automorphic spectral measure are not identified
(Remark~\ref{rem:moment-problem-vs-zero-location}).
The relationship between twisting morphisms and
scattering poles is \emph{not proved} in general.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Gap~B: arithmetic descent]%
\label{rem:langlands-gap-b}%
\index{Langlands programme!Gap B (arithmetic descent)}%
\index{function field!vs number field}%
\ClaimStatusOpen{}
The entire framework of this monograph operates over
function fields: the base curve~$X$ is a smooth complex
algebraic curve, the factorization algebra
$\mathrm{Fact}_X(\cA)$ lives on $\Ran(X)$, and the
modular convolution algebra $\gAmod$ is defined using
configuration spaces over~$X$.  This is geometric
Langlands territory.

The arithmetic Langlands programme works over number
fields~$F$, where $X$ is replaced by
$\operatorname{Spec}(\mathcal{O}_F)$ and the
factorization structure is replaced by adelic
automorphic forms.  The descent from function field to
number field is the deepest open problem in the
Langlands programme and has been open since
Langlands's original letter to Weil (1967).

This monograph does not address arithmetic descent.
The shadow obstruction tower, the MC equation, and all five main
theorems are statements about chiral algebras on
complex curves.  The spectral continuation programme
produces $L$-functions from sewing data, but the
resulting $L$-functions are already known by other
methods (Hecke theory for lattice theta series,
Franc--Mason for rational VOAs): the bar-cobar
machine provides a new \emph{proof route} to known
$L$-functions, not new $L$-functions from new
automorphic objects over number fields.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Gap~C: formal vs convergent]%
\label{rem:langlands-gap-c}%
\index{Langlands programme!Gap C (analytic continuation)}%
\index{shadow tower!convergence}%
\ClaimStatusOpen{}
The shadow obstruction tower
$\Theta_\cA^{\le 2}, \Theta_\cA^{\le 3},
\Theta_\cA^{\le 4}, \ldots$
is a sequence of finite-order approximations to the
full MC element~$\Theta_\cA$.  The all-arity inverse
limit $\Theta_\cA = \varprojlim \Theta_\cA^{\le r}$
exists (Theorem~\ref{thm:recursive-existence}), but
its \emph{analytic} properties depend on the shadow
growth rate $\rho(\cA)$
(Definition~\ref{def:shadow-growth-rate}).

The Langlands programme needs $L$-functions, which are
non-perturbative analytic objects: meromorphic functions
on the complex $s$-plane satisfying a functional equation.
The shadow obstruction tower is perturbative: it is a formal power
series in the arity variable~$t$.  The passage from
formal to convergent requires the shadow radius of
convergence $1/\rho(\cA)$ to be positive.

For class~$\mathbf{G}$ (Gaussian) and
class~$\mathbf{L}$ (Lie/tree) algebras,
$\rho = 0$ and the tower terminates: convergence is
trivially satisfied.  For class~$\mathbf{M}$ (mixed)
algebras, $\rho > 0$ and convergence requires
$\rho < 1$.  This is verified for specific families
(Virasoro at $c > c^* \approx 6.125$, see
Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-radius}), but it is not universal.
For $c < c^*$, the shadow series diverges and the
analytic content of the tower is accessible only through
Borel summation
(Proposition~\ref{prop:carleman-virasoro}).

The analytic continuation from shadow data to
$L$-functions is therefore family-dependent and is not
a consequence of the algebraic MC equation alone.
The MC equation is an integrability condition ($D^2 = 0$);
it does not by itself produce analytic continuation
to the complex $s$-plane.
\end{remark}

% ============================================================
\subsection{Spectral continuation programme}
\label{subsec:concordance-spectral-continuation}
\index{spectral continuation programme}

Four results on the arithmetic content of the shadow obstruction tower:

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(1)~Depth decomposition}
(Theorem~\ref{thm:depth-decomposition}):
$d(\cA) = 1 + d_{\mathrm{arith}} + d_{\mathrm{alg}}$,
where $d_{\mathrm{arith}}$ counts holomorphic Hecke eigenforms
(critical lines) and $d_{\mathrm{alg}}$ is the homotopy defect
($A_\infty$ non-formality of bar cohomology,
Theorem~\ref{thm:ainfty-formality-depth}).
Lattice: $d_{\mathrm{alg}} = 0$.
Virasoro: $d_{\mathrm{alg}} = \infty$.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(2)~Stieltjes representation}
(Theorem~\ref{prop:shadow-spectral-measure}):
$G(t) = \int\!\log(1{-}\lambda t)\,d\rho(\lambda)$
with spectral measure $\rho$ determined by the MC element.
For Virasoro, $\rho = \delta(\lambda{+}6/c)$.
The shadow series is Borel summable; Carleman's condition
gives uniqueness (Proposition~\ref{prop:carleman-virasoro}).

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(3)~Hecke-equivariant MC element}
(Theorem~\ref{thm:spectral-continuation-bridge}):
for lattice VOAs, $\gAmod[V_\Lambda]$ carries a Hecke module
structure.  The Hecke--Mellin correspondence provides analytic
continuation of the shadow data to the complex $s$-plane,
resolving the structural obstruction
(Remark~\ref{rem:structural-obstruction}) for this class.
For non-lattice theories the obstruction persists:
the Rankin--Selberg map from the shadow spectral measure~$\rho$
to the automorphic spectral measure on the moduli space is
ill-conditioned (Remark~\ref{rem:moment-problem-vs-zero-location}).

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(4)~Sewing--shadow intertwining}
(Theorem~\ref{thm:sewing-shadow-intertwining}):
$F_1^{\mathrm{conn}}(q;\cA) = \sum_{r\ge2}
\operatorname{Sh}_r^{(1)}(\cA) \cdot \mathcal{G}_r(q)$.
The connected sewing determinant equals the Chern--Weil pairing
$\det(1-K_q) = \exp(-\langle\Theta_\cA,[E_\tau]\rangle)$
(Corollary~\ref{cor:shadow-fredholm}).
For lattice VOAs, the shadow spectral measure~$\rho$
and the automorphic spectral measure coincide via the
Hecke correspondence
(Corollary~\ref{cor:spectral-measure-identification}).

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(4a)~Shadow-moduli resolution}
(Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-moduli-resolution}):
$\prod_j(1-\lambda_j\,t(q))^{c_j} = \det(1-K_q)$.
At leading order: $t(q) = (c/6)(\prod(1{-}q^n)-1)$.
The shadow-moduli map~$t(q)$ is not an unknown: it is
explicitly determined by the sewing determinant.
The universality of~$G$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:universality-of-G}):
$F_1^{\mathrm{conn}} = G_\cA(t(q))$ where
$G$ depends only on~$\rho$ and $t$ depends only on
the moduli, achieving complete separation of algebraic and
geometric data.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(4b)~MC~$=$~Newton's identities for the shadow spectrum}
(Proposition~\ref{prop:mc-bracket-determines-atoms}):
the MC equation at all arities is equivalent to Newton's
identities relating the power-sum moments $\mu_r$ to the
elementary symmetric polynomials of the spectral atoms.
For two Satake-type atoms:
$p_r = e_1\,p_{r-1} - e_2\,p_{r-2}$.
Combined with modularity
(Proposition~\ref{prop:modularity-constraint}): atoms are
Hecke eigenvalues satisfying Petersson orthogonality.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(5)~Modular rigidity programme}
(\S\ref{sec:modular-rigidity}).
The shadow at arity~$r$ encodes
$\operatorname{Sym}^{r-1}$ data
(Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow-symmetric-power}).
Serre's reduction: automorphy of all
$\operatorname{Sym}^r \Rightarrow$ Ramanujan.
The MC equation provides all symmetric power moments;
the missing step is functorial transfer
$\mathrm{GL}(2) \to \mathrm{GL}(r{+}1)$ for $r \ge 5$
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:modular-spectral-rigidity}).
The bridge from MC to Ramanujan has four stations
(Remark~\ref{rem:mc-ramanujan-bridge}): MC/Newton (proved),
modularity/Hecke (proved),
Sym$^r$ continuation (open for $r \ge 5$),
Serre reduction (conditional).
The \emph{operadic Rankin--Selberg theorem}
(\S\ref{sec:operadic-rankin-selberg}) attacks the gap:
MC recursion on moment $L$-functions
(Theorem~\ref{thm:mc-recursion-moment}, PROVED)
$+$ CPS converse theorem hypotheses verified
(Theorem~\ref{thm:converse-hypotheses}, PROVED)
$\Rightarrow$ automorphy CONDITIONAL on prime-locality
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:prime-locality-transfer}; proved for lattice VOAs).
For lattice VOAs, the full chain closes: MC $\Rightarrow$
Deligne by a new route.
The \emph{Hecke--Newton closure}
(\S\ref{sec:hecke-newton-closure}) resolves prime-locality for
lattice VOAs via the Hecke module structure: the shadow amplitudes
are chiral graph integrals
(Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow-chiral-graph}), the MC recursion
preserves Newton's identities at each prime
(Theorem~\ref{thm:hecke-newton-lattice}), and
Corollary~\ref{cor:unconditional-lattice} gives an unconditional
new proof of the Ramanujan bound for lattice theta eigenforms.
For non-lattice theories, the precise obstruction is the
\emph{arithmetic of the OPE}: whether the graph integrals on
Hecke-translated curves factor through Satake parameters
(Remark~\ref{rem:non-lattice-gap}).
The \emph{prime-locality frontier}
(\S\ref{sec:prime-locality-frontier}) identifies four routes:
(A)~Hecke module extension (hard: $[d_{\mathrm{sew}}, T_p]$
exactness);
(B)~motivic route (Brown--Levin elliptic motives);
(C)~analytic route (most promising: MC rigidity
$+$ Carleman uniqueness transfers character-level Hecke
equivariance to shadow level);
(D)~computational route (Ising, Lee--Yang, Potts;
\textbf{result}: Proposition~\ref{prop:rational-cft-multiplicativity-failure}
proves that the partition function Dirichlet series of diagonal
rational CFTs is \emph{not} multiplicative ($14$ coprime failures
for Ising, $12$ for tricritical Ising, $14$ for three-state Potts,
all with $O(1)$ integer defects), ruling out naive Euler-product
prime-locality at the partition function level;
Proposition~\ref{prop:stieltjes-signed-universal} proves the
Stieltjes spectral measure is universally signed for all $c > -22/5$;
prime-locality, if it holds, must be formulated at the
shadow-projection level $\operatorname{Sh}_r(\Theta_\cA)$ rather
than the partition function).
The \emph{analytic continuation programme}
(\S\ref{sec:analytic-continuation-programme}) synthesizes
these into a single cohomological target: the Hecke
defect class $[\delta_p(\cA)] \in H^1(\gAmod,
\mathrm{ad}_{T_p})$
(Definition~\ref{def:hecke-defect-class}).
Vanishing of $[\delta_p]$ for all~$p$
$\Leftrightarrow$ prime-locality
$\Leftrightarrow$ Ramanujan
(Proposition~\ref{prop:hecke-defect-equivalences},
Theorem~\ref{thm:rigidity-inheritance}).
The scattering coupling factorization
(Theorem~\ref{thm:scattering-coupling-factorization})
and the structural separation theorem
(Theorem~\ref{thm:structural-separation})
prove that the MC equation at genus~$1$ \emph{exhausts} its
algebraic content: every consequence that is extractable
from the Rankin--Selberg pairing has been extracted, and the
zero-location question requires either higher-genus input
or genuinely analytic input external to the MC equation.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(5a)~Period filtration and motivic structure.}
Shadow coefficients are FM configuration-space periods
(Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow-periods}).
The depth decomposition is the motivic weight decomposition
(Remark~\ref{rem:motivic-decomposition}):
$d_{\mathrm{arith}}$ counts non-Tate summands $h^1(f_j)$,
$d_{\mathrm{alg}}$ is the depth of the Tate part.
The Virasoro shadow obstruction tower is a single Kummer motive $K(6/c)$
(Remark~\ref{rem:kummer-motive}).
The Weil analogy table
(Remark~\ref{rem:weil-analogy-table}) maps the Weil proof
to the MC equation: $\Theta = \mathrm{Frob}$,
$D^2=0 = \mathrm{Frob}^2=q$, shadow obstruction tower $=$ \'etale
cohomology, bracket positivity $=$ Hodge--Riemann.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(6)~Euler--Koszul classification}
(Definition~\ref{def:euler-koszul-tier},
Theorem~\ref{thm:euler-koszul-tier-classification}):
modular Koszul algebras are \emph{exact Euler--Koszul}
($D_\cA \equiv 1$; Heisenberg, $V_k(\fg)$, $\beta\gamma$),
\emph{finitely defective} ($D_\cA \neq 1$ but defect
polynomial; Virasoro, $\cW_N$), or
\emph{non-Euler--Koszul} (Epstein with class number $\geq 2$).
Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction sends exact to finitely defective:
arithmetically, ``Euler product minus finite harmonic defect''
(Remark~\ref{rem:ds-arithmetic-defect}).
Shadow depth $\kappa_d$ and Euler--Koszul class
$\operatorname{ek}$ are independent invariants
(Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-euler-independence}).
The genus-$1$ modular datum $D_1(\cA) = (\kappa,\,\Delta,\,K,\,Q,\,\kappa_d,\,\operatorname{ek})$ packages these into a single invariant (Definition~\ref{def:genus1-modular-datum}).

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(5)~Sewing--Hecke reciprocity}
(Theorem~\ref{thm:sewing-hecke-reciprocity}):
the two-variable $L$-object
$L_\cA(s,u) := \int_\cF^{\mathrm{reg}}
F_\cA^{\mathrm{conn}}\,E^*(\tau,s)\,
y^{u-2}\,dx\,dy$
\emph{collapses} to a one-variable object:
$L_\cA(s,u) = \Gamma(v)\,(2\pi)^{-v}\,S_\cA(v)$
where $v = s + u - 1$.
The collapse is exact: it follows from the fact that the
sewing operator is diagonal in the Fock basis
($F_\cA^{\mathrm{conn}}$ depends on $y$ alone),
so Rankin--Selberg unfolding converts the modular integral
into a Mellin transform.
At $u = 0$: Sewing--Selberg formula.
At $s = 1$: Dirichlet--sewing lift.
Zero-side and prime-side are locked by the
constraint $v = s + u - 1$.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(6)~Quartic residue programme}
(\S\ref{sec:quartic-residue-programme}):
the $3 \times 3$ Schur complement of the mixed
$(s,u)$-transform extracts the quartic contact coupling
(potential side) or the quartic resonance section (Gram side);
these are reciprocal (Theorem~\ref{thm:schur-complement-quartic}).
For Virasoro: $\Sigma_2 = Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}^{\mathrm{ct}}
= 10/[c(5c{+}22)]$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:virasoro-quartic-determinant}).
The genuine residue kernel~\eqref{eq:residue-kernel} has
decay exponent $-(c{+}\sigma{-}1)/2$ depending on
$\sigma = \operatorname{Re}(\rho)$, distinguishing on-line
from off-line zeros before any positivity argument.
The closure conjecture
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:quartic-closure})
asserts that the intersection of quartic
Gram-compatibility loci over all families, slices, central
charges, and regulators equals
$\{\rho : \operatorname{Re}(\rho) = 1/2\}$.
Four structural gaps remain
(\S\ref{sec:four-gaps}):
MC $\to$ Li (sign; structurally blocked by
Proposition~\ref{prop:li-criterion-failure}),
Euler product (spectral measure),
bar-cobar rigidity (Euler compatibility),
Nyman--Beurling (norm mismatch).
Root cause (Remark~\ref{rem:beilinson-four-gaps}):
all four reduce to the logical independence of
integrability ($D^2 = 0$) from positivity
(absolute value bounds).
Collapse permanence
(Proposition~\ref{prop:collapse-permanence},
Remark~\ref{rem:collapse-permanence}): the interacting
sewing kernel factors through $s{+}t$ at every arity;
the one-variable reduction is permanent.
Algebraic--analytic divide
(Remark~\ref{rem:algebraic-analytic-divide}): the MC
equation organises all algebraic data; analytic
conclusions require Deligne, Franc--Mason, or Langlands.
The operadic functorial transfer
(Remark~\ref{rem:overdetermination-honest}, route~(c))
is the only route that could make MC self-sufficient.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(6a)~Genus-$2$ arithmetic frontier}
(\S\ref{sec:genus2-arithmetic-frontier}):
the sewing--Hecke collapse is a genus-$1$ phenomenon: it
rests on Fock diagonality of the sewing operator, which
breaks at genus~$2$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:genus2-non-collapse}).
The genus-$2$ sewing kernel is a $2 \times 2$ block operator
with off-diagonal coupling through the internal seam; the
Fredholm determinant does not factor
(Proposition~\ref{prop:genus2-non-diagonal}).
The spectral decomposition on
$\mathrm{Sp}_4(\mathbb{Z})\backslash\mathfrak{H}_2$
includes Saito--Kurokawa lifts from genus-$1$ cusp forms,
providing an arithmetic bridge
(Remark~\ref{rem:saito-kurokawa-bridge}).
The genus-$2$ MC equation constrains the Saito--Kurokawa
projection through off-diagonal shadow data absent at
genus~$1$; whether this suffices to determine eigenvalues
(not only weights) is the central open problem
(Remark~\ref{rem:genus2-honest-assessment}).
This is the precise escape route from the structural
separation theorem
(Theorem~\ref{thm:structural-separation},
Remark~\ref{rem:genus2-escape-route}).
The \textbf{B\"ocherer bridge}
(Theorem~\ref{thm:bocherer-bridge},
\S\ref{subsec:bocherer-bridge-theorem})
makes this escape explicit: for even unimodular lattices
with $\mu(\Lambda) \geq 4$, the genus-$2$ cusp component
is nonzero
(Proposition~\ref{prop:leech-cusp-nonvanishing});
via the refined B\"ocherer conjecture
(Dickson--Pitale--Saha--Schmidt, proved),
this cusp component factors through central $L$-values
$L(1/2, \pi_f \times \chi_D)$, providing the first
algebraic access from MC data to the critical line
$\operatorname{Re}(s) = 1/2$.
Escalation to genus~$g$ accesses
$L(1/2, \operatorname{Sym}^{g-1} f)$, implementing
Serre's programme
(Remark~\ref{rem:bocherer-escalation}).
The \textbf{Leech $\chi_{12}$-projection}
(Theorem~\ref{thm:leech-chi12-projection}):
$c_2 \neq 0$, the Leech lattice projects nontrivially
onto $\chi_{12} = \mathrm{SK}(f_{22})$
($\dim S_{12}(\mathrm{Sp}(4,\bZ)) = 1$, no ambiguity).
Via Waldspurger: MC data determines
$L(11, f_{22} \times \chi_D)$ for all fundamental $D < 0$.
\textbf{Chriss--Ginzburg realization}
(Remark~\ref{rem:chriss-ginzburg-bocherer}):
the chain $D^2{=}0 \to \Theta_\cA \to \Theta^{(2)}
\to c_2 \to L$-values is a sequence of projections
of the single MC element through the modular convolution
algebra $\mathfrak{g}_\cA^{\mathrm{mod}}$,
the genus-$2$ three-shell decomposition, and the
shadow extraction (Corollary~\ref{cor:shadow-extraction}).
The genus-$2$ Beurling kernel
(Remark~\ref{rem:genus2-beurling-kernel})
narrows Gap~D: the spectral-support mismatch between
sewing and Nyman--Beurling is eliminated at genus~$2$.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(6b)~Finite Miura defect at genus one}
(\S\ref{sec:miura-defect-decomposition}):
Theorem~\ref{thm:finite-miura-defect} proves the vacuum
character splitting $\chi_{\cW_N} = \chi_\cH^{N-1}
\prod_{m=1}^{N-1}(1-q^m)^{N-m}$, the connected free energy
splitting, and the Dirichlet defect
$D_{\cW_N}^{\mathrm{prime}} = -\zeta(u{+}1)\sum_{m=1}^{N-1}(N{-}m)m^{-u}$
at three equivalent levels.  The finite defect principle
(Remark~\ref{rem:finite-defect-principle}):
the Heisenberg core is quartically blind; all quartic
resonance data live in the finite defect sector.
Defect unification (Conjecture~\ref{conj:defect-unification}):
the prime-side defect
(Proposition~\ref{prop:prime-side-defect-formula})
and the zero-side defect
$D_{\cW_N}^{\mathrm{res}}$
(Definition~\ref{def:zero-side-miura-defect})
are both genus-$1$ shadows of the same bar-intrinsic MC correction.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(6c)~Residue clutching defect}
(\S\ref{sec:residue-clutching-defect}):
the proved clutching law
(Theorem~\ref{thm:nms-clutching-law-modular-resonance})
is applied to the residue divisor.
The residue clutching defect $K_{\cA,\rho,\xi}$
(Definition~\ref{def:residue-clutching-defect})
measures whether the residue Gram determinant at a
candidate zero~$\rho$ satisfies the same boundary
compatibility as the MC-derived resonance class.
Conjecture~\ref{conj:clutching-closure}: $K = 0$ for all
families and boundary strata iff $\operatorname{Re}(\rho) = 1/2$.
This is strictly stronger than the quartic closure conjecture
and uses the full nonlinear modular structure.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(6d)~Beilinson functional}
(\S\ref{sec:beilinson-functional}):
the scalar aggregation
$\cB^{\mathrm{glob}}(\rho) = \sum_{\cA,v}\int
\cB_{\cA,v}\,d\mu_\cA$ vanishes iff both cubic and quartic
residue data match MC shadows on all slices.
Closure hierarchy: clutching $\Rightarrow$ Beilinson
$\Rightarrow$ quartic.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(6d$'$)~The Koszul--Epstein frontier.}
Whether the extra structure of shadow-metric Epstein zetas
(MC constraints from $D^2 = 0$, bar-cobar symmetry from
Theorem~B, clutching law from Mok's degeneration formula)
forces critical-line zeros is the central open question of
the arithmetic programme.
The Li/Weil/positivity route is dead: the Nyman--Beurling
criterion requires Hilbert-space completeness that the
MC data alone does not provide
(Theorem~\ref{thm:structural-separation}).
The clutching route
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:clutching-closure}) is the surviving
path: it uses the full nonlinear modular structure
(the boundary stratification of~$\overline{\cM}_g$,
the planted-forest corrections, the residue Gram
determinant) rather than scalar positivity conditions.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(6e)~Miura--packet bridge}
(\S\ref{sec:miura-packet-bridge}):
Proposition~\ref{prop:miura-packet-splitting} splits the
$\cW_N$ packet connection into a diagonal Heisenberg core
and a defect connection.  The Heisenberg core is
arithmetically inert: diagonal, universal zeta divisors,
no contribution to the frontier defect form
(Remark~\ref{rem:heisenberg-inert}).  All obstructions to
matching automorphic scattering reduce to the finite defect
sector.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(7)~Gram positivity}
(Theorem~\ref{thm:gram-positivity},
Theorem~\ref{thm:interacting-gram-positivity}):
the sewing inner product
$\langle f,g\rangle_\cA = \sum_N a_\cA(N)f(N)g(N)$
has reproducing kernel $K_\cA(s,t) = S_\cA(s{+}t)$.
Its Gram matrix $\mathscr{M} = V^T\!DV \succ 0$
(Vandermonde with positive sewing weights).
Interacting corrections from the shadow spectral
measure $\rho = \sum c_j\delta(\lambda_j)$ preserve
positivity unconditionally when all atoms $\lambda_j < 0$
(the unitary case, including Virasoro with $c > 0$).
The resonance locus is confined to non-unitary $c < 0$.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(8)~Shadow resonance locus}
(Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-resonance-locus}):
$\mathcal{R} = \{(c,\alpha) :
\det\mathscr{M}^{\mathrm{int}} = 0\}$
is empty for $c > 0$ (unitary); confined to $c < 0$
(non-unitary).  Lee--Yang $c = -22/5$ is the first
entry.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(9)~Motivic weight}
(Remark~\ref{rem:motivic-weight-ek}):
$\operatorname{ek} = 0$ $\Leftrightarrow$ sewing
kernel is pure Tate.
$\operatorname{ek} = e$ $\Leftrightarrow$ mixed Tate
of depth~$e$.
DS reduction $=$ motivic truncation.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(10)~Ramanujan bound for lattice eigenforms, Deligne-free}
(Theorem~\ref{thm:ramanujan-deligne-free}):
twelve-station proof using MC + HS-sewing + CPS + Jacquet-Shalika + Serre.
No $\ell$-adic cohomology.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(11)~Ramanujan bound for rational VOAs}
(Theorem~\ref{thm:non-lattice-ramanujan}):
extends to diagonal modular invariants via Franc-Mason
vector-valued Hecke theory on the character vector.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(12)~Ramanujan bound for irrational VOAs}
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:irrational-ramanujan}):
\emph{conditional} on Langlands functoriality for all symmetric
powers ($r \geq 5$).  Extends to arbitrary central charge via
the Roelcke--Selberg spectral theorem as infinite-dimensional
Hecke theory.  Scope: all chirally Koszul algebras with HS-sewing.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(13)~Self-dual factorisation}
(Theorem~\ref{thm:self-dual-factorization}):
\ClaimStatusProvedHere{}
for chirally Koszul self-dual $\cA \simeq \cA^!$ with
$Z_\cA \in M_k(\Gamma_0(N))$, the constrained Epstein zeta
factors into $d(\cA)-1$ standard automorphic $L$-functions.
Five-step proof: Verdier involution, functional equation,
Hecke eigenform decomposition (multiplicity one),
standard $L$-functions, GRH (conditional).
Steps~1--4 unconditional.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(14)~Verdier--Hecke commutation}
(Theorem~\ref{thm:hecke-verdier-commutation}):
\ClaimStatusProvedHere{}
at genus~$1$, Verdier duality~$\bD$ commutes with
Hecke correspondences~$T_p$ for $p\nmid N$.
Proof via dual isogeny bijection on~$\cM_{1,1}$
and sublattice bijection for lattice VOAs.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(15)~Theta decomposition bridge}
(Proposition~\ref{prop:theta-bridge-rational}):
\ClaimStatusProvedHere{}
for minimal models $\cM(p,q)$ with diagonal modular invariant,
characters decompose via Rocha--Caridi into theta functions
at level~$2pq$, giving Dirichlet $L$-functions modulo~$2pq$.
Resolves the non-lattice gap
(Remark~\ref{rem:non-lattice-gap}) for all rational VOAs.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(16)~Newton--shadow--Hecke correspondence}
(Proposition~\ref{prop:newton-shadow-hecke}):
\ClaimStatusProvedHere{}
shadow power sums $p_r = r\cdot S_r$ determine Hecke eigenvalues
via Newton's identities.  The MC equation at arity~$4$ is
structurally parallel to the Hecke relation
$T_2^2 = T_4 + p^{k-1}T_1$.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(17)~Davenport--Heilbronn principle}
(Remark~\ref{rem:davenport-heilbronn-koszul}):
the Davenport--Heilbronn phenomenon (off-line zeros of
non-unimodular Epstein zeta) is explained by failure of
Koszul self-duality: $h(D) > 1$ iff
$V_\Lambda \not\simeq V_{\Lambda^*}$ iff the Verdier
involution does not fix~$Z$.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(18)~Arithmetic packet connection}
(Definition~\ref{def:arithmetic-packet-connection};
Theorem~\ref{thm:packet-connection-flatness};
Proposition~\ref{prop:gauge-criterion-scattering}):
the depth decomposition $d(\cA) = 1 + d_{\mathrm{arith}} + d_{\mathrm{alg}}$
is realised as a flat meromorphic connection
$\nabla_\cA^{\mathrm{arith}}$ on the arithmetic packet
module~$M_\cA$ over the spectral line.  The singular divisor
$D_\cA = \bigcup_\chi\operatorname{div}(\Lambda_\chi)$
is independent of the nilpotent data: the arithmetic skeleton
controls the poles; the algebraic defect contributes only
unipotent monodromy.  The frontier defect form
$\Omega_\cA = d\log\Lambda_{\mathrm{Eis}} - d\log\varphi$
measures the discrepancy between the activated $L$-packets and
the automorphic scattering matrix; the gauge criterion
(Proposition~\ref{prop:gauge-criterion-scattering}) reduces
scattering access to exactness of~$\Omega_\cA$.
The arithmetic comparison conjecture
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:arithmetic-comparison})
posits that higher-genus MC data computes residues
of~$\Omega_\cA$ at scattering poles.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(19)~Classical sewing-to-zeta bridge}
\label{item:concordance-classical-sewing-zeta}%
\index{Riemann zeta function!from annular trace}%
\index{sewing!to completed zeta function}%
The Jacobi theta function $\vartheta(t) = \sum_{n\in\bZ}
e^{-\pi n^2 t}$ is the zero-mode lattice sum of the
rank-one self-dual lattice VOA~$V_\bZ$.  Its Mellin
transform, after clutching symmetrisation, is the
completed Riemann zeta function:
$\Xi_{\mathrm{ann}}(s) := \tfrac12 + \tfrac12 s(s{-}1)
\int_1^\infty \psi(t)(t^{s/2-1} + t^{(1-s)/2-1})\,dt
= \xi(s)$,
where $\psi(t) = (\vartheta(t)-1)/2$.
This is Riemann's 1859 computation: split the Mellin
integral at $t=1$, apply Poisson summation
$\vartheta(1/t) = t^{1/2}\vartheta(t)$ on the $(0,1)$
piece, and collect into the manifestly entire,
$s \leftrightarrow 1{-}s$ symmetric form.
Within the open/closed framework, $\vartheta$ arises as the
scalar annular resonance trace of the cyclic open
factorization category of~$V_\bZ$ on
$({\mathbb P}^1, \{0,\infty\})$, after determinant-line
trivialisation of the oscillator sector (i.e., passing from
the full character $q^{-1/24}/\eta \cdot \sum q^{n^2/2}$
to the zero-mode lattice sum alone).  The
clutching symmetry $\Xi(s) = \Xi(1{-}s)$
reflects the Poisson self-duality of the
$\bZ$-lattice, which is the abelian instance of
Koszul self-duality.  The nontrivial zeros
of~$\Xi_{\mathrm{ann}}$ are exactly those of~$\zeta(s)$.
\emph{This identity is classical and does not
constitute a new result of the programme.}
The genuine frontier is the nonlinear completion:
whether the modular shadows $\Theta_{\cA}^{(\geq 4)}$
from $\cW$-type theories deform zero statistics.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(20)~Entanglement-annulus conjecture}%
\label{item:concordance-entanglement-annulus}%
\index{entanglement!annulus conjecture}%
\ClaimStatusConjectured{}
For a cyclic open factorization dg-category
$C_{\mathrm{op}}$ on a tangential log curve with
modular twisting element~$\Theta_C$, the entanglement entropy
should admit a connected shadow expansion:
$S_{\mathrm{EE}}(C_{\mathrm{op}}) = \tfrac{c}{3}\log(L/\epsilon)
+ \sum_{r \geq 3} \Delta S_r$,
where the scalar term is the Calabrese--Cardy contribution
(already proved from $\kappa = c/2$ alone,
Chapter~\ref{chap:entanglement}), and
$\Delta S_r$ is the arity-$r$ connected annular clutching
coefficient of~$\Theta_C$.  The four-class
partition $({\mathbf G}, {\mathbf L}, {\mathbf C}, {\mathbf M})$
classifies entanglement corrections by shadow depth.
Three unproved hypotheses: (a)~replica annuli~$A_n$
realised inside the log-modular cooperad,
(b)~cyclic trace extends to the replica family,
(c)~factorisation of disconnected configurations.
For $\cW_3$, the first nonlinear correction
$\Delta S_4^{\mathrm{mod}}(\cW_3)$ is forced by the
composite $\Lambda = :TT: - \tfrac{3}{10}\partial^2 T$
and should be computable from
$R^{\mathrm{mod}}_{4,\mathrm{ann}}(\cW_3)$.
The complementarity theorem (Theorem~C) constrains the
higher-arity shadows of $\cA$ and $\cA^!$ via the
Verdier involution, but the constraint is \emph{not}
$\Theta_\cA + \Theta_{\cA^!} = 0$: at the scalar level,
$\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) + \kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}) = 13$
(AP24), and the full-tower relation is
$\mathbb{D}(\Theta_\cA) = \Theta_{\cA^!}$
(Verdier intertwining, not negation).
The complementarity sum
$S_{\mathrm{EE}}^{\mathrm{scalar}}(\mathrm{Vir}_c)
+ S_{\mathrm{EE}}^{\mathrm{scalar}}(\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c})
= \tfrac{26}{3}\log(L/\epsilon)$
follows from the proved $\kappa + \kappa' = 13$
identity, not from a conjectural
$\Theta + \Theta' = 0$.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(21)~Canonical cyclotomic boundary chart from root stacks}%
\label{item:concordance-cyclotomic-chart}%
\index{cyclotomic chart!canonical|textbf}%
\index{root stack!boundary chart|textbf}%
\index{admissible level!root-stack logarithmicity}%

The boundary algebra
$A_b = \operatorname{RHom}_{\mathcal{M}}(b, b)$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:thqg-local-global-bridge}(i))
depends on the choice of boundary vacuum~$b$.
Inner-automorphism approaches to constructing
boundary charts suffer from a $\sigma$-ambiguity:
conjugation by $\sigma \in \operatorname{Aut}(V_k)$
produces a gauge-equivalent but non-canonical chart.
Root stacks eliminate this ambiguity by making the
branching data geometric.

\emph{The $N$-th root stack at a puncture.}%
\index{root stack!definition|textbf}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere{}
Let $(X, D, \tau)$ be a tangential log curve
(Definition~\ref{def:tangential-log-curve}) with
$p \in D$ a puncture and $t$ a local coordinate at~$p$
($t(p) = 0$).  For $N \geq 1$, the \emph{$N$-th root
stack} of~$X$ at~$p$ is the Deligne--Mumford stack
\begin{equation}\label{eq:root-stack-def}
X_{p,N}
\;:=\;
\sqrt[N]{p/X}
\;\cong\;
\bigl[\operatorname{Spec}\bC[\![u]\!] \,/\, \mu_N\bigr]
\;\sqcup\;
(X \setminus \{p\}),
\end{equation}
where $u^N = t$ is the tautological $N$-th root
coordinate and $\mu_N$ acts by
$\zeta \cdot u = \zeta u$ for
$\zeta \in \mu_N = \langle e^{2\pi i/N}\rangle$.
The coarse moduli space of $X_{p,N}$ is~$X$ itself,
with the stacky structure concentrated at the single
point~$p$.  The structure morphism
$\pi_N \colon X_{p,N} \to X$
is an isomorphism away from~$p$ and a
$\mu_N$-gerbe at~$p$.  The orbifold line bundle
$\mathcal{L}_p^{1/N} := \pi_N^* \mathcal{O}_X(p)^{1/N}$
on~$X_{p,N}$ has the property that
$(\mathcal{L}_p^{1/N})^{\otimes N} \cong
\pi_N^* \mathcal{O}_X(p)$;
its space of sections carries a canonical
$\mu_N$-eigenspace decomposition indexed by
$j \in \bZ/N\bZ$.
This is standard algebraic geometry
(Cadman~2007;
Abramovich--Graber--Vistoli~2008).

\emph{The cyclotomic boundary chart.}%
\index{cyclotomic chart!general construction}
\ClaimStatusConjectured{}
Let $\cA$ be a chiral algebra on~$X$ with a module
category~$\mathcal{M}$ supported at~$p$.
The pullback $\pi_N^* \cA$ is a
$\mu_N$-equivariant chiral algebra on the root stack,
and the boundary vacuum acquires a canonical
$\bZ/N\bZ$-grading:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:cyclotomic-vacuum}
b^{\mathrm{cyc}}_{N}
\;:=\;
\bigoplus_{j \in \bZ/N\bZ}
\mathcal{L}_p^{j/N} \otimes \pi_N^* \mathcal{M}_0,
\end{equation}
where $\mathcal{M}_0$ is the vacuum object of~$\mathcal{M}$
and $\mathcal{L}_p^{j/N} = (\mathcal{L}_p^{1/N})^{\otimes j}$.
The \emph{cyclotomic boundary chart at order~$N$} is the
endomorphism algebra
\begin{equation}\label{eq:cyclotomic-chart}
A^{\mathrm{cyc}}_N
\;:=\;
\operatorname{RHom}_{X_{p,N}}(b^{\mathrm{cyc}}_N,\,
b^{\mathrm{cyc}}_N).
\end{equation}
This is a $\bZ/N\bZ$-graded $A_\infty$-algebra
whose grading is tautological: the $\mu_N$-action
on~$X_{p,N}$ induces a $\bZ/N\bZ$-grading on
morphism spaces by eigenvalue decomposition.
The graded components carry:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)},nosep]
\item \emph{sector idempotents}
$e_j \in A^{\mathrm{cyc}}_{N,(0)}$, one for
each $j \in \bZ/N\bZ$;
\item \emph{shift morphisms}
$s_j \colon e_j \to e_{j+1}$ in $A^{\mathrm{cyc}}_{N,(1)}$,
satisfying the \emph{nilpotent $N$-cycle relation}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:nilpotent-N-cycle}
s_{N-1} \circ \cdots \circ s_1 \circ s_0
\;=\;
t \cdot \operatorname{id}_{e_0},
\end{equation}
which vanishes on the special fibre $t = 0$;
\item \emph{fractional-mode expansions}:
fields $\phi(z)$ of the pullback
$\pi_N^* \cA$ admit mode expansions in
$u = t^{1/N}$, giving fractional modes
$\phi_{m/N}$ for $m \in \bZ$.
\end{enumerate}
For $N = 1$, this recovers the ordinary (ungraded)
boundary chart
$A_b = \operatorname{RHom}(b, b)$
of Theorem~\ref{thm:thqg-local-global-bridge}.
The nilpotent $N$-cycle \eqref{eq:nilpotent-N-cycle}
forces the open-sector category
$C^{\mathrm{op}}_N := \operatorname{Perf}(A^{\mathrm{cyc}}_N)$
to be nonsemisimple for $N > 1$: the shift morphisms
generate non-split extensions between sector objects.
The construction eliminates the $\sigma$-ambiguity of
inner-automorphism approaches: $N$ and the
$\mu_N$-action are geometric data of the root stack,
not choices of automorphism.

\emph{(21a)~Specialisation to admissible levels.}%
\label{item:concordance-cyclotomic-admissible}%
\index{admissible level!cyclotomic chart}%
\ClaimStatusConjectured{}
For $\cA = V_k(\fg)$ at admissible level
$k = -h^\vee + p/q$ with $p, q$ coprime, the
canonical choice of root stack order is $N = q$
(the denominator of the shifted level $k + h^\vee$).
The $q$-root stack
$D^{(q)} := \sqrt[q]{p/X}
\cong [\operatorname{Spec}\bC[\![u]\!]/\mu_q]$
with $u^q = t$ then provides the cyclotomic boundary
chart $A^{\mathrm{cyc}}_{k,q}$ with a
$\bZ/q\bZ$-graded quasi-lisse (QLS) structure.
The denominator~$q$ is geometrised: it is the
order of the stacky isotropy group at~$p$, not an
external combinatorial parameter.
Logarithmicity of the representation category
$\mathcal{O}_k$ at admissible~$k$ is encoded in
the root-boundary geometry of the $q$-fold cover.
Chiral quadratic duality (Gui--Li--Zeng) applied to the
QLS chart produces a canonical $q$-periodic
twisted pair and CDG algebra.
Comparison to the nonsemisimple KL category is proved for
$\fg = \mathfrak{sl}_2$ (McRae--Yang;
Creutzig--McRae--Yang);
for general~$\fg$ it is a comparison theorem to be proved.

\emph{(21b)~Affine Weyl orbit periodicity for Kac--Moody algebras.}%
\label{item:concordance-cyclotomic-km}%
\index{affine Weyl group!root-stack periodicity}%
\index{Kac--Moody algebra!cyclotomic chart}%
\ClaimStatusConjectured{}
For $\cA = V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_N)$ at admissible level
$k = -N + p/q$, the affine Weyl group
$\mathcal{W} = W \ltimes Q^\vee$
acts on the set of admissible weights
$\operatorname{Adm}_k$ with quotient by
$q Q^\vee$-translations
(Theorem~\ref{thm:kw-bar-general-rank}).
The $q$-root stack provides a geometric
realisation of this quotient periodicity: the
$\bZ/q\bZ$-grading on $A^{\mathrm{cyc}}_{k,q}$
corresponds to the coset decomposition
$Q^\vee / q Q^\vee \cong (\bZ/q\bZ)^r$
(where $r = \operatorname{rank}(\fg)$),
and the fractional
modes $J^a_{m/q}$ of the affine currents
generate the $q$-block decomposition of the
admissible category
$\mathcal{O}_k^{\mathrm{adm}}$.
At integer level ($q = 1$), the root stack is
trivial and the boundary chart is ungraded: the
integrable category $\mathcal{O}_k^{\mathrm{int}}$
is semisimple with no block structure, consistent
with the absence of cyclotomic periodicity.

The root stack does \emph{not} recover the full
affine Weyl group $\mathcal{W}$: it captures only
the finite quotient
$Q^\vee / q Q^\vee$ that controls
the periodicity of Weyl orbits on admissible weights.
The infinite part of $\mathcal{W}$ (the lattice
$Q^\vee$ itself) acts on the Verma-module labels
within each block and is visible in the BGG resolution
(Theorem~\ref{thm:bgg-from-bar}), not in the
cyclotomic grading.

\emph{(21c)~Virasoro self-duality and the second root stack.}%
\label{item:concordance-cyclotomic-virasoro}%
\index{Virasoro algebra!self-duality at c=13@self-duality at $c=13$}%
\index{root stack!second, Virasoro}%
\ClaimStatusConjectured{}
The Koszul involution
$c \mapsto 26 - c$ for the Virasoro algebra
is a $\bZ/2$-symmetry of the family
$\{\operatorname{Vir}_c : c \in \bC\}$,
with fixed point $c = 13$
(uncurved-quadratic self-duality;
see AP8 for the distinction from the
Feigin--Frenkel involution at $c = 0$).
At $c = 13$,
$\operatorname{Vir}_{13}^! \cong \operatorname{Vir}_{13}$
and the complementarity asymmetry
$\delta_\kappa = \kappa - \kappa' = c/2 - (26-c)/2 = c - 13$
vanishes.  We conjecture that this
family-level $\bZ/2$-symmetry admits a geometric
realisation via the second root stack:
\[
X_{p,2} = \sqrt[2]{p/X}
\cong [\operatorname{Spec}\bC[\![u]\!] / \mu_2],
\qquad u^2 = t,
\]
with the $\mu_2$-action exchanging the two sheets
of the double cover.  At $c = 13$, the cyclotomic
boundary chart $A^{\mathrm{cyc}}_{2}$ should carry
a $\bZ/2\bZ$-grading whose even part is the
self-dual boundary algebra and whose odd part
encodes the Koszul pairing
$\langle \cA, \cA^! \rangle = \langle \cA, \cA \rangle$.
The shift morphism $s_0 \colon e_0 \to e_1$
intertwines the algebra with its dual; the nilpotent
relation $s_1 \circ s_0 = t \cdot \operatorname{id}$
degenerates on the special fibre, reflecting the
passage from the complementarity pairing to
its degeneration at the self-dual point.

At $c \neq 13$: the $\bZ/2$-symmetry is broken.
The two sheets $\operatorname{Vir}_c$ and
$\operatorname{Vir}_{26-c}$ are genuinely distinct
algebras, and the cyclotomic boundary chart
splits into two non-isomorphic sectors.
The complementarity asymmetry
$\delta_\kappa = c - 13 \neq 0$
measures the failure of the $\mu_2$-equivariant
structure.

\emph{Scope fence.}
The Virasoro $\bZ/2$-symmetry is the Koszul
involution on the \emph{family}
$\{c \mapsto 26 - c\}$, not a symmetry of
a single algebra at generic~$c$.
The root-stack realisation posits that this
family-level involution admits a geometric
incarnation as a stacky double cover at the
self-dual central charge.
This is analogous to the admissible-level story,
where the root stack order~$q$ comes from the
rational structure of the level; here, the
order~$2$ comes from the quadratic structure
of the Koszul duality relation $c + c' = 26$.

\emph{(21d)~The cyclotomic Zhu algebra and
Frenkel--Zhu theory.}%
\label{item:concordance-cyclotomic-zhu}%
\index{Zhu algebra!cyclotomic refinement}%
\index{Frenkel--Zhu theory!cyclotomic extension}%
\ClaimStatusConjectured{}
The Zhu algebra $A(V) = V / V \circ V$
(Zhu~\cite{Zhu96}; Frenkel--Zhu~\cite{FZ92})
controls the representation theory of a vertex
algebra~$V$: the functor $M \mapsto M/M_{>0}$
defines a bijection between simple
$V$\nobreakdash-modules and simple
$A(V)$\nobreakdash-modules.
For $V = V_k(\fg)$,
$A(V_k(\fg)) \cong U(\fg)$
(Frenkel--Zhu~\cite{FZ92}).

The root-stack construction refines the
Zhu functor as follows.
At level~$k$ with $N$-th root stack at~$p$,
the pullback $\pi_N^* V_k$ admits fractional
modes and the Zhu quotient inherits a
$\bZ/N\bZ$-grading:
\[
A^{\mathrm{cyc}}_N(V_k)
\;:=\;
\bigoplus_{j \in \bZ/N\bZ}
A(\pi_N^* V_k)_{(j)},
\]
where $A(\pi_N^* V_k)_{(j)}$ consists of
Zhu equivalence classes of vectors whose
$\mu_N$-eigenvalue is $e^{2\pi i j/N}$.
For $N = 1$: $A^{\mathrm{cyc}}_1(V_k) = A(V_k)
\cong U(\fg)$, ungraded.  For $N = q$ at
admissible $k = -h^\vee + p/q$: the grading
refines $U(\fg)$ into $q$ sectors, and the
representation theory of the graded algebra
$A^{\mathrm{cyc}}_q(V_k)$ should recover the
$q$-block structure of the admissible
category~$\mathcal{O}_k^{\mathrm{adm}}$.

The conjectured compatibility between the
cyclotomic Zhu algebra and the cyclotomic
boundary chart is the assertion that the natural map
$A^{\mathrm{cyc}}_N(V_k)
\to H^0(A^{\mathrm{cyc}}_N)$
(from the graded Zhu algebra to the degree-zero
cohomology of the boundary chart) is an
isomorphism of $\bZ/N\bZ$-graded algebras.
For $N = 1$, this reduces to the standard
identification $A(V_k) \cong H^0(A_b)$ that
underlies the Zhu functor.
For $N > 1$, it asserts that the root-stack
construction is compatible with the Zhu
truncation.

\emph{Scope fence.}
The cyclotomic Zhu algebra $A^{\mathrm{cyc}}_N(V_k)$
is well-defined for all~$N$ and all levels~$k$
(the Zhu quotient and the $\mu_N$-eigenspace
decomposition commute), but the representation-theoretic
content is non-trivial only when $N$ matches the
arithmetic of the level.  At integer level with
$N > 1$, the grading exists but does not
capture new representation-theoretic data beyond
what the ungraded Zhu algebra already sees.
The conjecture is that $N = q$ (the level
denominator) is the minimal order for which
the cyclotomic refinement captures genuinely new
structure (the block decomposition of the
admissible category).

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(21e)~Periodic curved dg structure at admissible levels}%
\label{item:concordance-periodic-cdg}%
\index{admissible level!periodic CDG structure|textbf}%
\index{curved dg algebra!periodic at admissible level}%
\index{logarithmic CFT!bar complex structure}%
\ClaimStatusConjectured{}
At admissible level $k = -h^\vee + p/q$ with $p, q$
coprime positive integers ($p \geq 2$), the simple
quotient $L_k(\fg)$
has a non-free PBW filtration: vacuum null vectors at
conformal weight~$pq$ force relations in the associated
graded.  The bar complex $\barBch(L_k(\fg))$ should
carry a \emph{periodic curved dg structure}: the
bar degree is $2p$-periodic
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:periodic-cdg}), and the
curvature element $m_0 \in \barBch(L_k(\fg))$
(which vanishes for the universal algebra $V_k(\fg)$
by Koszulness, but is nonzero for the simple quotient)
is nilpotent with period controlled by the numerator:
\[
  \barB^{n+2p}(L_k(\fg)) \cong \barB^n(L_k(\fg))
  \quad\text{for all } n \gg 0.
\]
The periodicity parameter is $2p$, where $p$ is the
numerator of $k + h^\vee = p/q$; this matches the
periodicity of
the small quantum group $u_q(\fg)$ at
$q = e^{\pi i q/p}$
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:kl-periodic-cdg}).
The curved dg structure is indexed by the
$\mu_q$-grading of the cyclotomic chart from
items~\textup{(21)--(21d)} above.

\emph{Meaning of periodic CDG.}
A curved dg coalgebra $(C, d, m_0)$ with $d^2 = [m_0, -]$
is \emph{periodic of period~$N$} if $C^{n+N} \cong C^n$
as CDG-coalgebras for all $n \gg 0$.
Equivalently, in Positselski's framework~\cite{Positselski11},
the coderived category $D^{\mathrm{co}}(C)$ reduces to
the stable category of a finite-dimensional quotient.
For the universal algebra $V_k(\fg)$, chirally Koszul
at all levels (Proposition~\ref{prop:pbw-universality}),
the bar complex is uncurved ($m_0 = 0$): no periodicity.
For the simple quotient $L_k(\fg)$ at admissible~$k$,
the bar complex acquires curvature from the vacuum null
vector, and the conjecture asserts this curved complex
is $2p$-periodic in bar degree.

\emph{The case $\fg = \mathfrak{sl}_2$.}
At $k = -2 + p/q$, the simple quotient $L_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$
is an admissible-level affine vertex algebra with
central charge $c = 1 - 6(p-q)^2/(pq)$;
its Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction is the
Virasoro minimal model $\cM(p,q)$.
The vacuum null vector in $L_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$
appears at conformal weight~$pq$.
Comparison to external constructions:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)},nosep]
\item Feigin--Tipunin (2010): the logarithmic
  extension $\overline{\cM}(p,q)$ has a
  $\bZ/q\bZ$-graded nonsemisimple module category
  with $q$~blocks, each a non-split extension of
  $p - 1$ simple modules.  The $\mu_q$-grading of the
  cyclotomic chart (item~(21a)) should recover
  this block decomposition; the $2p$-periodicity of
  the bar complex acts on each block.
\item Creutzig--Ridout~\cite{CreutzigRidout2013}: the
  Kazhdan--Lusztig-type category for $\mathfrak{sl}_2$
  at admissible level has a ribbon structure whose
  twist eigenvalues are roots of unity.  The CDG
  periodicity should intertwine with this ribbon
  structure through the cyclotomic boundary chart.
\end{enumerate}
These comparisons are \emph{verified only for
$\fg = \mathfrak{sl}_2$}: the block structure and
ribbon periodicity are explicitly computed in the
cited works.  For general~$\fg$, the
Kazhdan--Lusztig category at admissible level is
constructed (Arakawa~\cite{Arakawa2016RationalAdmissible};
Creutzig--McRae--Yang),
but the explicit CDG periodicity of the bar complex and
its comparison to the categorical $\mu_q$-grading are
not proved.

\emph{Overall scope fence for items
\textup{(21)--(21e)}.}
Four levels of the cyclotomic programme:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)},nosep]
\item The root stack construction \eqref{eq:root-stack-def}
  is standard algebraic geometry
  (\ClaimStatusProvedHere).
\item The cyclotomic boundary chart
  \eqref{eq:cyclotomic-chart} and its
  $\bZ/N\bZ$-grading are conjectural as
  boundary algebras for chiral algebras
  (\ClaimStatusConjectured).
\item The admissible-level specialisation,
  the Kac--Moody Weyl orbit periodicity,
  the Virasoro self-duality at $c = 13$,
  and the cyclotomic Zhu algebra are
  conjectural (\ClaimStatusConjectured).
\item The periodic CDG structure
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:periodic-cdg})
  is the deepest layer: it asserts that the
  cyclotomic grading of the boundary chart
  is reflected in the periodicity of the bar
  differential on the simple quotient.
\end{enumerate}
The construction of items \textup{(21a)--(21e)}
applies to the
\emph{simple quotient} $L_k(\fg)$, not the universal
algebra~$V_k(\fg)$.
The universal algebra is chirally Koszul at all levels
and its bar complex is uncurved.
The periodic CDG structure is the bar-complex
manifestation of logarithmic CFT: the
non-semisimplicity of the representation category is
encoded in the non-vanishing but nilpotent curvature
of the bar differential.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(22)~Modular globalisation conjecture and quartic first obstruction}%
\label{item:concordance-modular-globalisation}%
\index{modular globalisation!conjecture}%
\index{first obstruction!quartic}%
\ClaimStatusConjectured{}
Given the genus-zero skeleton
$S_0(A_b) = (A_b,\, C^*_{\mathrm{ch}}(A_b, A_b),\, A^!,\,
  r(z))$
of a boundary A$_\infty$-chiral algebra (incorporating
boundary chart, intrinsic bulk, line Koszul dual, and binary
line-OPE kernel), there should exist a filtered dg~Lie algebra
$\fg_X := \operatorname{Conv}(C^{\mathrm{oc,log}}_{\mathrm{mod}}
(X,D,\tau),\, \operatorname{End}(Z_{\mathrm{ch}}(C_{\mathrm{op}}),
A_b))$
such that modular completions of~$S_0(A_b)$ are precisely
MC elements $\Theta_C \in \MC(\fg_X)$, with the genus-zero part
recovering~$S_0(A_b)$.  The first obstruction to modular
globalisation lies in quartic filtration and is represented by
the image of the modular quartic resonance class
$[R^{\mathrm{mod}}_{4,g,n}]$ in
$H^2(\operatorname{gr}^4_F \fg_X)$.  This follows because cubic
gauge triviality
(Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:cubic-gauge-triviality}})
removes the cubic obstruction: the first cohomologically
nontrivial shadow is quartic.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(23)~Eight discard criteria}%
\label{item:concordance-discard-criteria}%
\index{discard criteria!eight permanent}%
Any proposed extension of the spectral continuation programme
\textup{(}items 1--18 above\textup{)} that violates one of the
following criteria is false:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(D\arabic*)},nosep]
\item Does not recover Beilinson--Drinfeld complementarity.
\item Treats bar-cobar or HTT as arithmetic/spectral rigidity
  (bar-cobar is homotopical, not spectral-positive).
\item Ignores Miura injectivity (Arakawa).
\item Proposes an un-regularised, un-factorisation-compatible,
  or non-line-valued universal shadow.
\item Places quartic rigidity in the Heisenberg core
  (Heisenberg is arithmetically transparent but quartically blind).
\item Compares residues only as scalars, ignoring clutching
  (the quartic resonance class is divisor-valued).
\item Relies on the $\zeta$-proxy that was shown to fail
  the safe-point test.
\item Seeks positivity on the modular \emph{curve} without
  a polarised geometric lift to a modular \emph{surface}
  (the Rankin--Selberg integral on a curve is not
  sign-preserving).
\end{enumerate}
The MC equation is a
\emph{flatness/integrability} condition; it does not imply
Li-type \emph{positivity} without additional structure
(a real form, a polarisation, or a positive trace).
The correct statement is: bar-cobar $+$ Euler compatibility
$+$ surface positivity $\Rightarrow$ critical-line rigidity
for the associated genus-$1$ $L$-object.

% ======================================================================
\section{Three falsification tests}
\label{sec:concordance-falsification-tests}
\index{falsification tests}
% ======================================================================

The five main theorems and the MC element
$\Theta_\cA$ rest on three structural pillars:
the local Swiss-cheese universal property,
the Drinfeld--Sokolov homotopy transfer to
Virasoro, and the convergence of the shadow obstruction tower.
Each pillar admits a decisive test.
If any one of these tests fails, the corresponding
component of the programme is wrong and must be
abandoned or rebuilt.  We state each test, its
failure mode, and the current evidence.

\medskip
\noindent
\textbf{(a) Local Swiss-cheese universal property for Heisenberg.}

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{Test.}\enspace
Compute the chiral Hochschild cochain complex
$C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cH_k, \cH_k)$
for the Heisenberg algebra~$\cH_k$ and verify the
universal open/closed pair
$U(\cH_k) = (C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cH_k, \cH_k),\;
\cH_k)$
of Theorem~\ref{thm:thqg-swiss-cheese}.
The Swiss-cheese structure on the pair should
reproduce the Heisenberg OPE:
$\alpha(z)\,\alpha(w) \sim k/(z-w)^2$.

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{Failure mode.}\enspace
If $C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cH_k, \cH_k)$ does not
carry the expected Swiss-cheese $\mathrm{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$
structure, or if the recovered OPE disagrees with the
standard Heisenberg OPE, then the local architecture
of the open/closed realization
(\S\ref{subsec:concordance-open-closed-realization})
is wrong.
The derived center would fail to be the universal
bulk for the simplest possible boundary algebra,
and the entire four-stage open/closed programme
(\S\ref{par:concordance-four-stage-architecture})
would collapse at stage~1.

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{Current evidence.}\enspace
The test passes.
Since $\cH_k$ has abelian Lie conformal algebra
$\mathfrak{h}_k$, the Chevalley--Eilenberg complex
is formal:
$C^*_{\mathrm{Lie}^*}(\mathfrak{h}_k)
= \mathrm{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathfrak{h}_k^*[1])$.
The chiral Hochschild cohomology
(Theorem~\ref{thm:heisenberg-obs})
is $\mathrm{ChirHoch}^*(\cH_k) \cong k[\Theta]$
with $|\Theta| = 2$, recovering the unique
nontrivial outer derivation $D(\alpha) = \mathbf{1}$.
The Swiss-cheese operations
$m_k^{\mathrm{SC}} = 0$ for $k \geq 3$
(class~G: Gaussian, shadow depth~$2$),
confirming that $\cH_k$ is Swiss-cheese formal.

\medskip
\noindent
\textbf{(b) DS--HPL transfer to Virasoro.}

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{Test.}\enspace
The Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction functor, applied to the
affine $\widehat{\fsl}_2$ dg-shifted Yangian data
$(m_2, r(z), \Delta)$ via homological perturbation,
should produce a well-defined Virasoro dg-shifted Yangian
at the chain level
(Vol~II, Theorem~\textup{thm:ds-hpl-transfer}).
The transferred $r$-matrix $r^{\mathrm{Vir}}(z)$
must satisfy the classical Yang--Baxter equation.
The transferred product $m_2^{\mathrm{Vir}}$ must
be associative up to homotopy controlled by $m_3$.

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{Failure mode.}\enspace
If the transferred $r$-matrix fails the CYBE, or if
the transferred product fails $A_\infty$ coherence,
then the gravity bridge is broken:
the passage from Kac--Moody dg-shifted Yangians
(where Koszul duality is well understood)
to Virasoro dg-shifted Yangians
(where the gravitational interpretation lives)
does not preserve the algebraic structure.
The DS reduction would not be a morphism of
modular Koszul datums, and the shadow cascade
$\Theta_{\Walg_N} = \mathrm{DS}(\Theta_{\widehat{\fg}})$
would fail to hold at the chain level.

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{Current evidence.}\enspace
The test passes at the binary level.
The gravitational coproduct $\Delta_z^{\mathrm{grav}}$
is proved strictly primitive at all arities
(ghost-number obstruction kills every HPL tree
correction).  The transferred binary $r$-matrix
inherits the CYBE from the affine source by the
intertwining property of the SDR
(strong deformation retract).
The $A_\infty$ coherence of $m_2^{\mathrm{Vir}}$
follows from the HTT (homotopy transfer theorem)
applied to the DS contraction.
At higher arities, the transfer is consistent
with the shadow cascade: the computed cubic and
quartic shadows of $\mathrm{Vir}_c$ match
those obtained by DS reduction from $\widehat{\fsl}_2$
at $c = 1 - 6(k-1)^2/k$.
The residual gap: a complete chain-level verification
of all $A_\infty$ operations $m_n^{\mathrm{Vir}}$
for $n \geq 4$ has not been carried out.

\medskip
\noindent
\textbf{(c) Shadow obstruction tower convergence for Virasoro.}

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{Test.}\enspace
The shadow growth rate
$\rho(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$
(Definition~\ref{def:shadow-growth-rate},
Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-radius})
must satisfy $\rho < 1$ for $c > c^*$,
where $c^*$ is the critical cubic root
$5c^3 + 22c^2 - 180c - 872 = 0$,
$c^* \approx 6.125$.
If $\rho \geq 1$ for all~$c$, the shadow obstruction tower
diverges everywhere and the MC element
$\Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}}$ does not exist as a
convergent object.

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{Failure mode.}\enspace
If $\rho(\mathrm{Vir}_c) \geq 1$ for all values
of~$c$, then the nonperturbative shadow partition
function
$Z^{\mathrm{sh}} = \sum_{g,r}
\mathrm{Sh}_r^{(g)} \, \hbar^{2g} \, t^r$
diverges at every point of the moduli space.
The shadow obstruction tower would be a formal
power series with zero radius of convergence,
and the modular MC element would exist only as
a pro-object, not as an honest element of the
completed convolution algebra.
The genus expansion $F_g(\mathrm{Vir}_c) =
\kappa \cdot \lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$
would remain valid (it uses only
$\Theta_\cA^{\le 2}$),
but the full shadow obstruction tower and all
higher-arity invariants would be
purely formal.

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{Current evidence.}\enspace
The test passes.
The shadow growth rate is
$\rho = \sqrt{9\alpha^2 + 2\Delta}\,/\,(2|\kappa|)$,
where $\alpha = S_3/\kappa$ and
$\Delta = 8\kappa S_4$ are the cubic and quartic
shadow invariants.  For Virasoro:
$\rho(\mathrm{Vir}_c) < 1$ for all $c > c^*$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-radius}); in particular,
$\rho(\mathrm{Vir}_{13}) \approx 0.467$ at the
self-dual point $c = 13$, and
$\rho \to 0$ as $c \to \infty$.
For $c < c^*$, the tower diverges
($\rho > 1$), but Borel summability holds
(Proposition~\ref{prop:carleman-virasoro}):
the shadow coefficients satisfy the Carleman
condition, so the formal series determines a
unique analytic function by Borel resummation.
The nonperturbative programme is therefore alive
for all~$c$, with two regimes:
convergent summation ($c > c^*$)
and Borel summation ($c < c^*$).
The critical value $c^* \approx 6.125$ separates
the two regimes but does not obstruct either.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{(5)~Analytic structure and resurgence}
(\S\ref{subsubsec:shadow-analytic-structure}--\ref{subsubsec:shadow-bootstrap-constraints}):
The scalar genus series has the closed form
$\kappa\bigl((\hbar/2)/\sin(\hbar/2) - 1\bigr)$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow-genus-closed-form}),
meromorphic in~$\hbar$ with simple poles at $2\pi n$.
The Borel transform in $u = \hbar^2$ is entire
(Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-borel-genus}); Stokes
multipliers are $\mathfrak{S}_n = (-1)^n 4\pi^2 n\kappa\,i$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow-stokes-multipliers});
the trans-series has instanton action $A = (2\pi)^2$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-transseries}).
The Liouville-transformed Schr\"odinger equation has
potential $V = 8\kappa^2\Delta/Q_L^2$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow-schwarzian}), with three
regular singular points for class~$\mathsf{M}$
(Corollary~\ref{cor:shadow-schrodinger-singularities}).
The one-loop WKB correction is the shadow connection
(Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow-wkb}(ii)); the classical
Voros half-period is universally $\pi$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow-voros-classical}).
Multi-channel shadows produce
Painlev\'e~VI (Remark~\ref{rem:painleve-multichannel}).
Status: all results \textsc{Green} (proved).

% ======================================================================
\section{Programme status ledger}
\label{sec:concordance-programme-ledger}
\index{programme status!ledger}
% ======================================================================

The following table classifies every major result
and programme by proof status.
\textsc{Green}: proved within this monograph
(local algebra, all hypotheses discharged).
\textsc{Amber}: externally supported or conditional
(physically motivated, with partial evidence,
but dependent on conjectural inputs or
physical interpretation).
\textsc{Red}: unproved global or modular descent
(genuine open problems with no current proof
strategy reducing to proved results).

\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.25}
\small
\begin{tabular}{cp{10.5cm}}
\textbf{Status} & \textbf{Result} \\
\hline
\multicolumn{2}{l}{\textsc{Green}
  \textup{(proved local algebra)}} \\[2pt]
& Theorems A--H
  (bar-cobar adjunction, inversion,
  complementarity, modular characteristic,
  Hochschild) \\
& MC1, MC2, MC4, MC5 (PBW, bar-intrinsic MC,
  strong completion towers, HS-sewing) \\
& MC3 proved for all simple types on the
  evaluation-generated core; DK-4/5
  (extension beyond evaluation modules) downstream \\
& Koszulness programme: $10$ unconditional
  equivalences $+$ $1$ conditional (Lagrangian)
  $+$ $1$ one-directional (D-module purity)
  \textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:koszul-equivalences-meta}\textup{)} \\
& Shadow obstruction tower algebraicity
  \textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:riccati-algebraicity}\textup{)} \\
& $\kappa$ formula universality: $\kappa(\cH_k) = k$,
  $\kappa(\widehat{\fg}_k) = \dim(\fg)(k{+}h^\vee)/(2h^\vee)$,
  $\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) = c/2$,
  $\kappa(\Walg_N) = c(H_N{-}1)$ \\
& $F_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$ for
  uniform-weight modular Koszul algebras at all genera
  \textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:genus-universality}\textup{)} \\
& Swiss-cheese theorem
  \textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:thqg-swiss-cheese}\textup{)} \\
& Chiral derived center as universal bulk \\
& Annulus trace
  \textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:thqg-annulus-trace}\textup{)} \\
& Heisenberg and lattice sewing
  \textup{(}Theorems~\ref{thm:heisenberg-sewing},
  \ref{thm:lattice-sewing}\textup{)} \\
& HS-sewing for the entire standard landscape (universal algebras)
  \textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:general-hs-sewing}\textup{)} \\
& All-arity inverse limit
  $\Theta_\cA = \varprojlim \Theta_\cA^{\le r}$
  \textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:recursive-existence}\textup{)} \\
& Algebraic-family rigidity
  \textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:algebraic-family-rigidity}\textup{)} \\
& DS primitivity of the gravitational coproduct
  (Vol~II, Theorem~\textup{thm:ds-hpl-transfer}) \\
& Epstein zeta of the shadow metric: functional equation
  for class~$\mathbf{M}$ at rational~$c$
  \textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-epstein-zeta}\textup{)} \\
& Shadow field $K_L = \bQ(\sqrt{\operatorname{disc}(Q_L)})$:
  imaginary quadratic for class~$\mathbf{M}$;
  trivial for class~$\mathbf{G}/\mathbf{L}$
  \textup{(}Remark~\ref{rem:shadow-field}\textup{)} \\
& Descent fan: three independent projections of
  $\Theta_\cA$ (categorical, spectral, modular)
  \textup{(}Proposition~\ref{prop:descent-fan}\textup{)} \\
& Lattice fan closure: all three projections
  compatible for lattice VOAs
  \textup{(}\S\ref{subsec:concordance-descent-fan}\textup{)} \\[4pt]
\multicolumn{2}{l}{\textsc{Amber}
  \textup{(externally supported, conditional,
  or physically interpreted)}} \\[2pt]
& Shadow CohFT
  \textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-cohft};
  equivariance and splitting proved;
  flat identity conditional on $|0\rangle \in V$,
  see AP30\textup{)} \\
& Gravitational interpretation of $\kappa$
  as central charge of the boundary graviton \\
& BTZ black hole entropy from the binary $r$-matrix \\
& Entanglement entropy $S_{\mathrm{EE}} = (c/3)\log(L/\epsilon)$
  from $\kappa$-level complementarity \\
& Holographic dictionary:
  bulk reconstruction from the derived center \\
& BV/BRST $=$ bar at higher genus:
  Heisenberg scalar level proved
  \textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:heisenberg-bv-bar-all-genera}\textup{)};
  general case conjectural
  \textup{(}Conjecture~\ref{conj:master-bv-brst}\textup{)} \\
& Shadow--chromatic correspondence
  \textup{(}Remark~\ref{rem:chromatic-shadow-correspondence}\textup{)} \\[4pt]
\multicolumn{2}{l}{\textsc{Red}
  \textup{(unproved global modular descent)}} \\[2pt]
& Multi-generator universality at $g \geq 2$:
  scalar formula \emph{fails}; cross-channel correction nonzero
  \textup{(}Open Problem~\ref{op:multi-generator-universality},
  resolved negatively\textup{)} \\
& Modular cooperad completion:
  full modular cooperad structure on the open
  factorization category
  $\mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{op}}$ \\
& Global open sector on tangential log curves
  \textup{(}modest globalisation over $(X,D,\tau)$\textup{)} \\
& Pixton ideal generation from class-M shadows
  \textup{(}Conjecture~\ref{conj:pixton-from-shadows}\textup{)} \\
& Arithmetic Langlands bridge:
  arithmetic descent from function field to
  number field
  \textup{(}Remark~\ref{rem:langlands-gap-b}\textup{)} \\
& Modular periodicity for simple quotients at
  admissible levels
  \textup{(}Conjecture~\ref{conj:modular-periodicity-minimal}\textup{)} \\
& D-module purity: converse direction
  \textup{(}item~(xii) of
  Theorem~\ref{thm:koszul-equivalences-meta}\textup{)} \\
& Shadow principal class: whether $Q_L$ always
  represents the principal ideal class
  \textup{(}Conjecture~\ref{conj:shadow-principal-class}\textup{)} \\
& Non-lattice $L$-function descent:
  sewing lift $\to$ $L$-function content for
  non-lattice algebras
  \textup{(}\S\ref{subsec:concordance-descent-fan}\textup{)}
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

% ----------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{The descent fan}
\label{subsec:concordance-descent-fan}
\index{descent fan|textbf}
\index{Theta_A@$\Theta_\cA$!descent fan}
% ----------------------------------------------------------------------

The MC element $\Theta_\cA$ projects onto three
mathematical worlds.  These projections share a common
source but do not compose into a single functor: the
``descent chain'' is a \emph{fan}, not a chain.

\begin{proposition}[Descent fan structure; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:descent-fan}
\index{descent fan!three projections}
The universal MC element $\Theta_\cA \in \MC(\gAmod)$
admits three independent projections with distinct targets
and distinct symmetries:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{Categorical projection.}
  $\cA \;\longmapsto\; \barBch(\cA) \;\longmapsto\; \cA^!$.
  Target: factorization coalgebras and their Verdier duals
  on $\Ran(X)$.
  Symmetry: the Koszul involution
  $\cA \leftrightarrow \cA^!$
  (Theorems~\textup{\ref{thm:bar-cobar-isomorphism-main}}
  and~\textup{\ref{thm:higher-genus-inversion}}).

\item \emph{Spectral projection.}
  $\cA \;\longmapsto\; \{S_r(\cA)\}_{r \ge 2}
  \;\longmapsto\; \sqrt{Q_L}
  \;\longmapsto\; \varepsilon^c_s(\cA)$.
  Target: the shadow obstruction tower, the algebraic function
  $\sqrt{Q_L}$ of degree~$2$
  (Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:riccati-algebraicity}}),
  and the constrained Epstein zeta
  (Construction~\textup{\ref{constr:shadow-epstein-eisenstein}}).
  Symmetry: the functional equation involution
  $s \mapsto c - 1 - s$
  of~$\varepsilon^c_s$
  \textup{(}eq.~\textup{\eqref{eq:constrained-epstein-fe}}\textup{)}.

\item \emph{Modular projection.}
  $\cA \;\longmapsto\; Z_g(\cA)
  \;\longmapsto\; S_\cA(v)$.
  Target: the genus expansion, the sewing lift~$S_\cA$, and
  the Rankin--Selberg integral over $\mathcal{F}$
  (Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:sewing-hecke-reciprocity}}).
  Symmetry: the Galois involution on the $L$-function
  content of~$S_\cA$.
\end{enumerate}
These three projections share $\Theta_\cA$ as common
source but do \emph{not} compose into a single functor.
The Koszul involution, the functional equation
involution, and the Galois involution are three
different involutions on three different spaces.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Items~(i) and~(ii) are projections of the proved MC
element $\Theta_\cA$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:mc2-bar-intrinsic}):
(i)~extracts the twisting morphism
$\alpha_\Theta \colon \barBch(\cA) \to \cA$ governing
Theorems~A and~B; (ii)~extracts the arity-$r$ shadow
coefficients $S_r$ and their generating function
$H(t)^2 = t^4 Q_L(t)$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:riccati-algebraicity}).
Item~(iii) extracts the genus-$g$ trace
$\mathrm{tr}\,\pi_{\mathrm{cl}}(\Theta_\cA)|_g$
and applies the sewing--Hecke collapse
(Theorem~\ref{thm:sewing-hecke-reciprocity}).
That the three projections have different targets
($\Ran(X)$-coalgebras, Dirichlet series, Rankin--Selberg
integrals) and different symmetry groups is immediate
from the construction.  That they do not compose: the
Koszul involution $\cA \mapsto \cA^!$ permutes the
source algebra, the functional equation acts on the
spectral variable~$s$, and the Galois involution acts
on the $L$-function coefficients; no functor
intertwines all three.
\end{proof}

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Proved levels.}\enspace
Projections~(i) and~(ii) are theorems: the categorical
projection is Theorems~A and~B, and the spectral
projection is Riccati algebraicity
(Theorem~\ref{thm:riccati-algebraicity}) composed with
the shadow--spectral correspondence
(Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-spectral-correspondence}).
The modular-to-arithmetic descent (from the sewing
lift~$S_\cA(v)$ to the $L$-function content) is
proved for lattice VOAs
