(Theorem~\ref{thm:hecke-newton-lattice},
Corollary~\ref{cor:unconditional-lattice})
and open for non-lattice algebras.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{False claims.}\enspace
Two natural conjectures are \emph{false}:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item ``The Koszul involution $\cA \mapsto \cA^!$
  descends to a functional equation on~$S_\cA(u)$.''
  \emph{False}: the sewing lift~$S_\cA(v)$ is
  determined by the shadow coefficients~$\{S_r\}$
  and the sewing operator, both of which depend on
  the full OPE data of~$\cA$.  The Koszul dual~$\cA^!$
  has different OPE data ($c \mapsto 26 - c$ for
  Virasoro), and $S_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}(v)$ forgets~$c$
  at the level of the functional equation of the
  constrained Epstein zeta.  The Koszul involution
  acts on the source algebra, not on the spectral
  variable.

\item ``The self-dual point $c = 13$ of the Koszul
  involution corresponds to the critical line
  $\operatorname{Re}(s) = 1/2$.''
  \emph{False}: the Koszul self-duality
  $\mathrm{Vir}_{13}^! \cong \mathrm{Vir}_{13}$
  is a statement about algebras; the critical line
  is a statement about zeros of~$\zeta$.  No
  mathematical relation between these two loci
  has been established.  The four structural gaps
  of~\S\ref{sec:four-gaps}
  (Remark~\ref{rem:beilinson-four-gaps}) quantify
  the logical distance.
\end{enumerate}

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Lattice closure.}\enspace
\ClaimStatusProvedHere{}
For lattice VOAs $V_\Lambda$, all three projections
are compatible and the fan closes to a triangle:
the Hecke--Newton closure
(Theorem~\ref{thm:hecke-newton-lattice}) identifies
the shadow obstruction tower coefficients with theta-function
Fourier coefficients, the Epstein zeta factors into
Hecke $L$-functions
(Theorem~\ref{thm:e8-epstein},
Proposition~\ref{prop:leech-epstein}),
and the sewing lift recovers the same $L$-function
data via the Rankin--Selberg integral.  The Koszul
involution, the functional equation, and the Hecke
action are mutually compatible because the lattice
theta function simultaneously controls all three.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Non-lattice irreducibility.}\enspace
\ClaimStatusOpen{}
For non-lattice algebras (Virasoro, $\Walg_N$, generic
affine Kac--Moody), the fan structure is irreducible:
no single involution governs all three projections,
and the descent from the sewing lift to $L$-function
content requires external arithmetic input
(Deligne's theorem, Franc--Mason modularity, or
Langlands functoriality; see
Remark~\ref{rem:algebraic-analytic-divide}).

\begin{construction}[Shadow Epstein functor]
\label{constr:shadow-epstein-functor}
\index{shadow Epstein functor|textbf}
\index{Epstein zeta!from shadow metric}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere{}
The spectral projection of the descent fan extends to
a functor from shadow metrics to $L$-functions.  Given
the shadow metric $Q_L(t) = (2\kappa + 3\alpha t)^2
+ 2\Delta\, t^2$
(Definition~\textup{\ref{def:shadow-metric}}),
define the constrained Epstein zeta
$\varepsilon^c_s(\cA) := \sum_{\Delta \in S}
(2\Delta)^{-s}$
via the spectral data extracted from the coefficients
of~$Q_L$.  This assignment is functorial: it respects
direct sums
(Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:independent-sum-factorization}})
and carries the functional equation
\textup{(}eq.~\textup{\eqref{eq:constrained-epstein-fe}}\textup{)}.
For lattice VOAs with class number~$1$, the constrained
Epstein zeta decomposes into Hecke $L$-functions of the
underlying number field.  For class number $h(D) \ge 2$,
the Epstein zeta is a finite sum of Hecke $L$-functions
weighted by genus characters; the identification of
$\varepsilon^c_s(\cA)$ with the zeta function
$\zeta_K(s)$ of the ring of integers requires the class
number computation and is not automatic.
\end{construction}

\begin{remark}[Four-layer algebraic--analytic stratification]%
\label{rem:four-layer-stratification}%
\index{algebraic--analytic stratification|textbf}%
\index{bar complex!algebraic--analytic layers}%
The descent fan articulates a clean stratification of the
mathematical content of~$\Theta_\cA$ into four layers of
increasing analytic depth:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{@{}clp{7.5cm}@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Layer} & \textbf{Name} & \textbf{Content} \\
\midrule
$0$ & Pure algebra & Bar complex, MC equation, shadow obstruction tower,
  CohFT structure, depth classification.
  All determined by OPE data; no integration over
  moduli required. \\[2pt]
$1$ & Algebraic intersection & Genus-$g$ free energies
  $F_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$ via the
  $\hat{A}$-genus, Mumford--GRR on the Hodge bundle.
  Integration over~$\bar{\mathcal{M}}_g$ but only
  against tautological classes. \\[2pt]
$2$ & Mixed & Hecke decomposition of shadow data
  (detected algebraically via Newton identities),
  Epstein zeta~$\varepsilon^c_s$ (algebraic from $Q_L$),
  functional equation (algebraic).  The spectral
  parameter~$s$ is analytic; the constraints on it
  are algebraic. \\[2pt]
$3$ & Genuinely analytic & Partition function
  $Z(\tau, \bar\tau)$ on the modular surface,
  Fredholm sewing determinant, Rankin--Selberg unfolding,
  scattering matrix $\varphi(s)$, zero locations
  of~$\zeta(s)$.  Requires analytic continuation
  off the real spectral axis. \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The bar complex and MC element live in Layer~$0$.
The genus expansion lives in Layer~$1$.
The Koszul--Epstein function lives in Layer~$2$.
The primary spectrum and partition function live in
Layer~$3$.  The structural obstruction
(Remark~\ref{rem:structural-obstruction}) is the
statement that no mechanism within Layers~$0$--$2$
reaches Layer~$3$: algebraic constraints on the
spectral line cannot determine the zeros of~$\zeta(s)$,
which live at complex spectral parameters.
\end{remark}

% ======================================================================
\section{Open problems in the \texorpdfstring{$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$}{Theta-oc} framework}
\label{sec:concordance-open-problems-theta-oc}
\index{open problems!Theta-oc framework@$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ framework|textbf}
\index{Maurer--Cartan element!open/closed!open problems|textbf}
% ======================================================================

The open/closed MC element
$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA = \Theta_\cA + \sum_j \mu^{\mathcal{M}_j}$
(Construction~\ref{constr:thqg-oc-mc-element},
Theorem~\ref{thm:thqg-oc-mc-equation})
packages the closed-sector genus tower, the open-sector module
operations, the bulk-to-boundary coupling, and the clutching
sewing data into a single MC element in the open-closed
convolution algebra
$\mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{oc}}_{\cA, \vec{\mathcal{M}}}$.
Every proved theorem in the monograph is a projection of
$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:thqg-oc-projection},
Proposition~\ref{prop:five-theorems-mc-projections}).
Each open problem is therefore a question about a specific
projection, extension, or structural property of
$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ that has not yet been established.

This section reformulates the principal open problems
in terms of $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$.  The purpose
is precision: a vague ``does $X$ hold?''\ becomes a
specific assertion about a projection, a coefficient,
a cohomology class, or a functorial property of a
well-defined algebraic object.

\subsection{Closed-sector projections}

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\arabic*)}]

\item \textbf{Multi-generator universality at $g \geq 2$}
  (Open Problem~\ref{op:multi-generator-universality},
  \textbf{resolved negatively}).

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Original statement.}
  For a multi-weight modular Koszul algebra~$\cA$
  (generators of distinct conformal weights), does
  $\mathrm{obs}_g(\cA) = \kappa(\cA) \cdot \lambda_g$ hold
  at all genera $g \geq 2$?

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Resolution.}
  \textbf{No.}
  Theorem~\ref{thm:multi-weight-genus-expansion} proves that
  the genus-$g$ free energy decomposes as
  $F_g(\cA) = \kappa(\cA) \cdot \lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}
  + \delta F_g^{\mathrm{cross}}(\cA)$,
  where $\delta F_g^{\mathrm{cross}}$ is a graph sum over
  mixed-channel boundary graphs.  The correction is generically
  nonzero: for $\cW_3$ at genus~$2$,
  $\delta F_2 = (c{+}204)/(16c) \neq 0$
  (Computation~\ref{comp:w3-genus2-cross-graphwise}).
  The scalar formula holds if and only if the algebra is
  uniform-weight or the cross-channel correction vanishes
  at each genus individually.

  The structural diagnosis: algebraic-family rigidity
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:algebraic-family-rigidity}) gives
  $\Theta_\cA^{\min} = \eta \otimes \Gamma_\cA$, but the
  Kuranishi map vanishes by parity, so the MC equation does
  not force $\Gamma_\cA = \kappa(\cA)\Lambda$.  The
  tautological-purity identification fails because the
  multi-channel graph sum includes mixed-channel amplitudes
  that produce contributions outside the $\kappa\Lambda$ line.

\item \textbf{BV/BRST $=$ bar at higher genus}
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:master-bv-brst}).

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Partial resolution.}
  For the Heisenberg algebra $\cH_\kappa$, the scalar-level
  identification
  $F_g^{\mathrm{BV}}(\cH_\kappa)
  = F_g^{\mathrm{bar}}(\cH_\kappa)
  = \kappa\cdot\lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$
  is proved at all genera via the Quillen anomaly formula,
  the Grothendieck--Riemann--Roch theorem on the universal curve,
  and the Faber--Pandharipande intersection formula
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:heisenberg-bv-bar-all-genera}).

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Original statement (general case).}
  The BV/BRST quantization of a holomorphic-topological field
  theory, at genus $g \geq 1$, coincides with the bar complex
  construction.

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ reformulation.}
  The open/closed MC element $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ is
  constructed algebraically via the bordered FM compactification
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:thqg-oc-mc-equation}).  The BV/BRST
  quantization produces a second MC element
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{BV}}_T \in \MC(\mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{BV}}_T)$
  in the BV convolution algebra.  The conjecture asserts an
  identification of convolution algebras
  \[
    \mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{oc}}_{\cA}\big|_{g \geq 1}
    \;\simeq\;
    \mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{BV}}_T\big|_{g \geq 1}
  \]
  under which $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ maps to
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{BV}}_T$.  At genus~$0$, the identification is
  the content of the PVA descent theorems D2--D6 (all proved in
  Vol~II).  The genus $\geq 1$ extension requires the analytic
  hypotheses (H1)--(H4) and the BV functor bridge
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:vol2-bv-functor-bridge}).

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Additional input.}
  The gap is the construction of a comparison map between the
  algebraic bordered FM integrals (which define
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$) and the BV path-integral
  quantization on $\Sigma_g$ at higher genus.  The analytic
  comparison theorem
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:analytic-algebraic-comparison}) establishes
  this for graph amplitudes; the missing step is the BV master
  equation on the full moduli space $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$,
  not only on individual graphs.

\item \textbf{Pixton ideal generation from class-M shadows}
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:pixton-from-shadows}).

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Original statement.}
  For class-M algebras ($r_{\max} = \infty$), the infinite
  family of MC-descended tautological relations generates the
  Pixton ideal in $R^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n})$.

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ reformulation.}
  The genus-$g$ component of the closed MC equation
  $D\Theta_\cA + \tfrac{1}{2}[\Theta_\cA, \Theta_\cA]
  + \hbar\Delta(\Theta_\cA) = 0$
  is a relation in
  $R^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)
  \otimes \Defcyc(\cA)$.
  The tautological projection
  $\operatorname{taut}_g \colon
  H^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g, \Defcyc(\cA))
  \to R^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)$
  sends each genus-$g$ MC identity to a tautological relation.
  The conjecture asserts:
  \begin{quote}
  \emph{The ideal generated by
  $\{\operatorname{taut}_{g,n}
  ([\Theta_\cA]_{g,n}) :
  g \geq 0,\, n \geq 0,\, \cA \in \text{class M}\}$
  equals the Pixton ideal.}
  \end{quote}
  Proved for semisimple Frobenius data
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:planted-forest-structure}(vi))
  via the Givental--Teleman--PPZ chain.  Open for non-semisimple
  data (logarithmic/admissible algebras).

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Strategy from $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$.}
  The open sector of $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$
  provides boundary-marked tautological classes
  $\operatorname{taut}_{g,n}^{\mathrm{oc}}$, which are
  strictly richer than the closed-sector classes.
  The four-sector decomposition of the MC equation
  produces relations with both interior and boundary
  markings.  These additional relations may generate
  the full Pixton ideal even when the
  closed-sector relations alone do not, because the
  open sector accesses descendant pairings (e.g.\
  $\int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{2,1}}
  \delta_{\mathrm{pf}}\,\psi_1^2$) that reveal
  shadow coefficients invisible in the closed
  $(g,0)$ projection.

\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Koszulness programme}

\begin{enumerate}[resume, label=\textup{(\arabic*)}]

\item \textbf{D-module purity: converse direction}
  (item~(xii) of Theorem~\ref{thm:koszul-equivalences-meta}).

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Original statement.}
  The forward direction
  ``D-module purity $\Rightarrow$ FM boundary acyclicity (Koszulness)''
  is proved.  Does the converse hold: does Koszulness of
  the bar factorization coalgebra imply D-module purity?

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ reformulation.}
  D-module purity of $\barBch(\cA)$ on $\Ran(X)$ is a regularity
  condition on the closed projection
  $\pi_{\mathrm{cl}}(\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA)$: it asserts
  that the bar differential, viewed as a $D$-module map on the
  Ran space, has holonomic kernel and cokernel.  Chiral
  Koszulness is bar concentration:
  $H^n(\barBch(\cA)) = 0$ for $n \geq 3$.  The question
  becomes:
  \begin{quote}
  \emph{Does holonomicity of the $D$-module structure of
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ on $\Ran(X)$ force
  cohomological concentration of the underlying cochain
  complex?}
  \end{quote}

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Additional input.}
  The forward direction uses the PBW spectral sequence; the
  converse would require showing that D-module regularity
  constrains the $E_2$ page of that spectral sequence to
  degenerate.  No proof strategy is currently available.

\item \textbf{Chiral Koszulness of simple quotients at admissible levels}
  (\S\ref{subsec:concordance-true-frontier}, item~1).

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Original statement.}
  The universal algebra $V_k(\fg)$ is chirally Koszul at all
  levels (Proposition~\ref{prop:pbw-universality}).
  Is the simple quotient $L_k(\fg)$ chirally Koszul at
  admissible levels?

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ reformulation.}
  The MC element $\Theta_{V_k}^{\mathrm{oc}}$ is well-defined
  for the universal algebra.  The simple quotient
  $L_k(\fg) = V_k(\fg)/J_k$ acquires a curved bar complex
  $\barBch(L_k)$ with curvature element $m_0$ from the
  vacuum null vector.  The question is whether
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_{L_k}$ exists as an MC element in the
  curved open-closed convolution algebra: that is, whether the
  curved bar complex $\barBch(L_k)$ has cohomology concentrated
  in bar degree~$1$ despite the curvature.  In $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$
  terms:
  \begin{quote}
  \emph{Does the quotient map $V_k \to L_k$ induce a morphism
  of open-closed MC elements
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_{V_k} \to \Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_{L_k}$
  in the coderived sense, with the target MC element
  well-defined in the periodic CDG convolution algebra
  $($Conjecture~\textup{\ref{conj:periodic-cdg}}$)$?}
  \end{quote}

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Strategy from $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$.}
  The Li--bar spectral sequence
  (Construction~\ref{constr:li-bar-spectral-sequence}) and the
  associated-variety criterion
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:associated-variety-koszulness}) provide a
  geometric test: the $E_2$ page of the spectral sequence is
  controlled by the reduced associated variety
  $X_{L_k} = \operatorname{Spec}(R_{L_k}/\sqrt{0})$.
  The $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ framework suggests studying the
  image of $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_{V_k}$ under the quotient
  functor, which detects nilpotent contributions from the
  nilradical of~$R_{L_k}$.

\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Categorical and completion targets}

\begin{enumerate}[resume, label=\textup{(\arabic*)}]

\item \textbf{Categorical modular Koszul duality}
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:categorical-modular-kd}).

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Original statement.}
  The curved bar-cobar adjunction at genus~$g$ induces an
  equivalence
  $\mathsf{D}^{\mathrm{co}}
  (\barB^{(g)}(\cA)\text{-}\mathsf{comod})
  \simeq
  \mathsf{D}^b(\cA\text{-}\mathsf{mod}^{\Sigma_g})$.

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ reformulation.}
  The open sector of $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ at genus~$g$
  defines a functor
  $\Phi_g^{\mathrm{oc}} \colon
  \cA\text{-}\mathsf{mod}^{\Sigma_g}
  \to
  \barB^{(g)}(\cA)\text{-}\mathsf{comod}$
  by twisting the $A_\infty$-module structure
  $\mu^{\mathcal{M}}$ with the genus-$g$ curvature
  $\kappa(\cA) \cdot \omega_g$.  The conjecture asserts that
  this functor, composed with the coderived passage, is an
  equivalence.  In $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ terms:
  \begin{quote}
  \emph{Is the genus-$g$ component of the open/closed MC
  equation sufficient to produce a quasi-inverse
  $\Psi_g^{\mathrm{oc}}$ to $\Phi_g^{\mathrm{oc}}$ in the
  coderived category?}
  \end{quote}
  At $g = 0$ this is Theorem~B.  The genus $\geq 1$
  extension requires controlling the curvature obstruction
  in the coderived sense, which is the
  content of the categorical lift.

\item \textbf{Modular cooperad completion}
  (ledger: \textsc{Red}).

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Original statement.}
  Construct the full modular cooperad structure on the open
  factorization category $\mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{op}}$: all genera,
  all boundary conditions, full sewing compatibility.

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ reformulation.}
  The MC equation for $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ is proved at
  all genera (Theorem~\ref{thm:thqg-oc-mc-equation}).  The
  annulus trace (Theorem~\ref{thm:thqg-annulus-trace}) verifies
  the genus-$1$ open-sector structure.  The cooperad completion
  asks for higher-genus open-sector structure maps
  $\delta_{g,n}^{\mathrm{op}} \colon
  \mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{op}} \to
  \mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{op}}^{\otimes n}$
  satisfying the modular cooperad axioms.  In
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ terms:
  \begin{quote}
  \emph{Does the clutching sector
  $\hbar\Delta_{\mathrm{clutch}}(\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA)$
  of the MC equation induce a modular cooperad structure on
  $\mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{op}}$ whose
  cocompositions are compatible with the genus tower?}
  \end{quote}
  The MC equation provides the necessary identities; the missing
  step is the categorical construction of cocomposition
  maps from iterated clutching on bordered FM compactifications.

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Strategy from $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$.}
  The four-sector decomposition of the MC equation
  produces, at each $(g,n)$, a compatibility condition
  between the open and closed sectors.  The genus-$g$
  clutching identity
  $\xi^*(\Theta^{(g)}) = \sum_{g_1+g_2=g}
  \Theta^{(g_1)} \star \Theta^{(g_2)}$
  is proved (Theorem~\ref{thm:mc2-bar-intrinsic}(iii)).
  The cooperad axiom (coassociativity) would follow from the
  associativity of the bordered FM clutching maps, once
  these are constructed for all stable topological types.

\item \textbf{Grand completion conjecture}
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:grand-completion}).

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Original statement.}
  The modular cumulant transform $\cA \mapsto M(\cA)$ extends
  finite-stage chiral Koszul duality to an equivalence of
  homotopy theories.

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ reformulation.}
  The five-component datum
  $M(\cA) = (\operatorname{Cum}_c(\cA),\, D_\cA,\,
  \tau_\cA,\, r_\cA(z),\, \Theta_\cA)$
  is a sequence of projections of
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$: cumulant coalgebra from the bar,
  coderivation from the differential, twisting morphism from the
  collision residue, $r$-matrix from the ordered boundary,
  modular logarithm from the full closed projection.  The
  conjecture asserts:
  \begin{quote}
  \emph{The open/closed MC element
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ is the universal object from which
  all five components of $M(\cA)$ are recovered, and the
  functor $\cA \mapsto \Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ is an
  equivalence on the completion closure of admissible
  chiral $A_\infty$-algebras.}
  \end{quote}

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Additional input.}
  The genus-$0$ truncation of $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ is
  completed bar-cobar (proved by MC4).  The ordered-boundary
  truncation is the dg-shifted Yangian jet tower (accessible
  windowwise by the jet principle,
  Conjecture~\ref{conj:jet-principle}).  The full equivalence
  requires the cumulant recognition
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:cumulant-recognition}): that the
  resonance-graded associated graded of $\hat{B}(\cA)$ is the
  cumulant coalgebra.

\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Bridge and factorization targets}

\begin{enumerate}[resume, label=\textup{(\arabic*)}]

\item \textbf{Factorization-categorical DK bridge}
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:derived-drinfeld-kohno}).

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Original statement.}
  The $\Eone$-factorization categories of the Yangian
  $\mathcal{Y}(\fg)$ and the quantum group $U_q(\fg)$ are
  equivalent.

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ reformulation.}
  The genus-$0$ ordered-boundary projection of
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ is the $r$-matrix
  $r_\cA(z) = \operatorname{Res}^{\mathrm{coll}}_{0,2}(\Theta_\cA)$
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:collision-residue-twisting}).
  The DK bridge asserts that the $\Eone$-monoidal structure on
  the module category induced by the $r$-matrix sector of
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ coincides with the braided monoidal
  structure from the factorization quantum group.
  In $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ terms:
  \begin{quote}
  \emph{Does the $\Eone$-monoidal functor induced by the
  ordered-boundary projection
  $\pi_{\mathrm{ord}}(\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA)$
  extend from evaluation modules to all of category~$\mathcal{O}$,
  and does it identify with the Latyntsev factorization
  quantum group?}
  \end{quote}
  The evaluation-locus theorem
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:factorization-dk-eval}) is the statement
  that the ordered-boundary MC element is correct on generators.
  The extension to all of $\mathcal{O}$ is a thick-generation
  problem about the ordered-boundary sector of
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$.

\item \textbf{DS--KD intertwining for arbitrary nilpotent}
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:ds-kd-arbitrary-nilpotent}).

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Original statement.}
  Bar-cobar duality commutes with Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction
  at arbitrary nilpotent~$f$.

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ reformulation.}
  The DS reduction functor
  $\mathrm{DS}_f \colon V_k(\fg) \to \mathcal{W}_k(\fg, f)$
  should induce a morphism of open-closed convolution algebras
  $\mathrm{DS}_f^{\mathrm{oc}} \colon
  \mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{oc}}_{V_k}
  \to
  \mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{oc}}_{\mathcal{W}_k(\fg,f)}$
  satisfying:
  \begin{quote}
  \emph{$\mathrm{DS}_f^{\mathrm{oc}}
  (\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_{V_k(\fg)})
  = \Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_{\mathcal{W}_k(\fg,f)}$.}
  \end{quote}
  In words: DS reduction is a morphism of modular Koszul datums.
  This is proved for principal~$f$; for hook-type in type~$A$
  it is conditional on DS-bar compatibility
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:hook-transport-corridor}).  The general case
  reduces to filtration formality ($E_1$-degeneration of the
  Kazhdan filtration spectral sequence) of the BRST complex
  (Remark~\ref{rem:ds-kd-formality-route}).  The
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ formulation makes the target precise:
  the MC element must be preserved under a specific morphism
  of convolution algebras, which is stronger than commutativity
  of functors.

\item \textbf{Modular factorization adjunction}
  (the modular extension of the factorization envelope adjunction).

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Original statement.}
  The modular factorization envelope $U^{\mathrm{mod}}_X$ is
  left adjoint to the modular primitive-current functor
  $\operatorname{Prim}^{\mathrm{mod}}$.

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ reformulation.}
  The six-fold modular Koszul datum
  $\Pi_X(L) = (\mathcal{F}_X(L),\, \bar{B}_X(L),\, \Theta_L,\,
  \mathcal{L}_L,\, (V^{\mathrm{br}}_L, T^{\mathrm{br}}_L),\,
  R^{\mathrm{mod}}_4(L))$
  is extended by the open/closed data to the eight-fold
  completed modular Koszul datum $\Pi^{\mathrm{oc}}_X(\cA)$
  (Definition~\ref{def:thqg-completed-platonic-datum}).  The
  adjunction asserts that
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ is \emph{universal} among MC
  elements in open-closed convolution algebras over cyclically
  admissible Lie conformal algebras:
  \begin{quote}
  \emph{For any modular Koszul algebra~$\cA$ with underlying
  Lie conformal algebra~$L$, is
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$
  the image under $U^{\mathrm{mod}}_X$ of the canonical
  MC element on~$L$?  Does the universality of the open sector
  yield the adjunction?}
  \end{quote}

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Additional input.}
  The genus-$0$ version of the adjunction is the classical
  factorization-envelope construction
  (Nishinaka~\cite{Nish26}).  The modular extension requires
  showing that the genus tower of $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$
  is functorially determined by the Lie conformal algebra data
  alone.  The bar-intrinsic construction
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:mc2-bar-intrinsic}) provides existence;
  the adjunction is the claim that the construction is
  \emph{universal} in a precise categorical sense.

\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Analytic and holographic targets}

\begin{enumerate}[resume, label=\textup{(\arabic*)}]

\item \textbf{Analytic realization criterion}
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:analytic-realization}).

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Original statement.}
  A unitary full VOA satisfying conformal OS, polynomial spectral
  growth, and HS-sewing admits a sewing envelope, a conformally
  flat 2-disk algebra, and a higher-genus coderived shadow.

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ reformulation.}
  The algebraic MC element $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ lives in
  the formal convolution algebra.  The analytic realization asks
  for a completed MC element
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}, \mathrm{an}}_\cA
  \in \MC(\hat{\mathfrak{g}}{}^{\mathrm{oc},\mathrm{an}}_\cA)$
  in an analytic completion of the open-closed convolution algebra,
  such that:
  \begin{quote}
  \emph{The inclusion
  $\mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA \hookrightarrow
  \hat{\mathfrak{g}}{}^{\mathrm{oc},\mathrm{an}}_\cA$
  sends $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ to
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc},\mathrm{an}}_\cA$, and the analytic
  MC element produces convergent genus-$g$ amplitudes for all
  $g \geq 0$ via trace-class sewing operators.}
  \end{quote}
  For Heisenberg and lattice VOAs, this is proved
  (Theorems~\ref{thm:heisenberg-sewing}
  and~\ref{thm:lattice-sewing}).  The general case requires
  constructing the analytic topology on
  $\mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ from the HS-sewing condition.

\item \textbf{Boundary bar duality}
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:boundary-bar-duality}).

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Original statement.}
  For analytically Koszul~$\cA$, completed boundary modules at
  genus~$0$ are equivalent to analytic comodules over
  $\barB^{\mathrm{an}}(\cA)$.

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ reformulation.}
  The open projection
  $\pi_{\mathrm{op}}(\Theta^{\mathrm{oc},\mathrm{an}}_\cA)$
  defines $A_\infty$-module operations
  $\mu_n^{\mathrm{an}}$ on completed boundary modules.
  The conjecture asserts that the twisting morphism
  $\alpha_{\Theta^{\mathrm{an}}}$
  (the genus-$0$ collision residue of the analytic MC element)
  induces the Koszul duality equivalence in the completed/analytic
  setting:
  \begin{quote}
  \emph{Does the analytic open-sector projection of
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc},\mathrm{an}}_\cA$ define an equivalence
  between completed $\cA$-modules and analytic
  $\barB^{\mathrm{an}}(\cA)$-comodules, extending Theorem~B
  from the algebraic to the analytic setting?}
  \end{quote}
  At curved genus ($g \geq 1$), the correct target is the
  coderived category of analytic contramodules.

\item \textbf{Boundary-defect realization}
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:boundary-defect-realization}).

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Original statement.}
  The dg-shifted Yangian $r_\cA(z)$ is realized as the
  boundary-defect operator product for a line defect in the
  bulk HT theory.

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ reformulation.}
  The $r$-matrix is the genus-$0$ binary collision residue of the
  closed projection:
  $r_\cA(z) = \operatorname{Res}^{\mathrm{coll}}_{0,2}(\Theta_\cA)$.
  The boundary-defect realization asks for a physical construction
  of the mixed projection
  $\pi_{\mathrm{mix}}(\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA)\big|_{0,1,n}$
  via a line defect:
  \begin{quote}
  \emph{Is there a line defect $\mathcal{L}$ in the bulk HT theory
  whose coupling to the boundary reproduces the mixed-sector
  projection of $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$, with the binary
  component giving $r_\cA(z)$?}
  \end{quote}
  The holographic modular Koszul datum
  $\mathcal{H}(T)$ packages the answer: the line category
  $\mathcal{C}$ is the mixed-projection receptacle, and the
  boundary-defect realization identifies line operators with
  mixed-sector components of $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$.

\item \textbf{Singular-fiber descent for minimal models}
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:singular-fiber-descent}).

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Original statement.}
  The modular Koszul datum for minimal models $\cM(p,q)$
  (as simple quotients of $\mathrm{Vir}_c$) is recovered by
  singular-fiber specialization from the universal Virasoro datum.

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ reformulation.}
  At generic~$c$, the MC element $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}$
  is well-defined.  At $c = c(p,q)$, the vacuum null vector
  forces a quotient $\mathrm{Vir}_c \to \cM(p,q)$, and the MC
  element acquires curvature.  The conjecture asserts:
  \begin{quote}
  \emph{The singular-fiber limit
  $\lim_{c \to c(p,q)} \Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}$
  exists in the coderived open-closed convolution algebra and
  equals $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_{\cM(p,q)}$.}
  \end{quote}
  This is a degeneration statement: the MC element has a
  well-defined limit under specialization of the central charge,
  and the limit is the MC element of the quotient.

\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Arithmetic targets}

\begin{enumerate}[resume, label=\textup{(\arabic*)}]

\item \textbf{Modular spectral rigidity}
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:modular-spectral-rigidity}).

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Original statement.}
  The MC equation provides all symmetric-power moments of shadow
  eigenvalues.  Does functorial transfer
  $\mathrm{GL}(2) \to \mathrm{GL}(r{+}1)$ for $r \geq 5$
  hold?

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ reformulation.}
  The shadow at arity~$r$ is the closed-sector projection
  $\pi_{\mathrm{cl}}(\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA)\big|_{r}$,
  which encodes $\operatorname{Sym}^{r-1}$ data
  (Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow-symmetric-power}).  The MC
  equation at all arities is equivalent to Newton's identities
  for the shadow spectrum
  (Proposition~\ref{prop:mc-bracket-determines-atoms}).  The
  conjecture asks:
  \begin{quote}
  \emph{Do the Newton's identities imposed by the MC equation
  $D\Theta_\cA + \tfrac{1}{2}[\Theta_\cA, \Theta_\cA] = 0$
  at all arities suffice to prove automorphy of all symmetric-power
  $L$-functions of the shadow spectral atoms?}
  \end{quote}
  The answer is yes for lattice VOAs
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:hecke-newton-lattice}) and no in general
  without additional analytic input (prime-locality transfer).
  The structural separation theorem
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:structural-separation}) shows that the
  genus-$1$ MC equation exhausts its algebraic content; the
  question is whether the full genus tower of
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ provides the missing analytic input
  via higher-genus Hecke constraints.

\item \textbf{Arithmetic comparison conjecture}
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:arithmetic-comparison}).

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Original statement.}
  The MC element $\Theta_\cA$ canonically determines the
  arithmetic packet connection $\nabla^{\mathrm{arith}}_\cA$,
  and higher-genus MC data accesses residues of the frontier
  defect form~$\Omega_\cA$.

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ reformulation.}
  The arithmetic packet connection
  $\nabla^{\mathrm{arith}}_\cA$ on the module $M_\cA$ over the
  spectral $s$-line is defined from the shadow spectral measure.
  The conjecture asserts a canonical map from the closed-sector
  tower to the connection:
  \begin{quote}
  \emph{The genus-$g$ components of
  $\pi_{\mathrm{cl}}(\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA)$
  for $g \geq 2$ determine the residues of the frontier defect
  form $\Omega_\cA$ at scattering poles, via the genus-$g$
  Saito--Kurokawa projection and the B\"ocherer bridge
  $($Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:bocherer-bridge}}$)$.}
  \end{quote}
  The genus-$2$ case is the first nontrivial instance: the
  three-shell decomposition of $\Theta_\cA|_{g=2}$ produces
  the Siegel modular form whose Fourier coefficients encode
  central $L$-values
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:leech-chi12-projection}).

\item \textbf{Shadow--Siegel gap for $K3 \times E$}
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-siegel-gap}).

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Status: PROVED (\S\ref{sec:bkm-k3e}).}
  The shadow obstruction tower of $K3 \times E$ does not
  produce the Igusa cusp form $\Phi_{10}$.  Four independent
  obstructions are identified: categorical (number vs function),
  modular characteristic ($\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}} = 3 \neq 5 = \kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}$),
  second quantization (single-copy vs DMVV symmetric product),
  and Schottky at $g \geq 4$ ($\mathrm{codim} = (g{-}2)(g{-}3)/2$).
  The Borcherds multiplicative lift
  $\operatorname{Borch}(2\,\phi_{0,1}) = \Phi_{10}$ is the
  genus-$1 \to 2$ bridge; at genus~$2$ the Torelli map is
  birational, so $F_2 = 7/1920$ is the topological residue of
  $1/\Phi_{10}$.  The four $\kappa$ invariants
  ($\kappa(\cA) = 3$, $\kappa_{\mathrm{BCOV}} = 0$,
  $\kappa_{\mathrm{MacMahon}} = 0$, $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}} = 5$)
  are tabulated in Remark~\ref{rem:four-kappas}, extending the
  polysemy analysis of Remark~\ref{rem:kappa-polysemy}.

  Ten structural results for $K3 \times E$
  (\S\ref{sec:k3-chiral-algebra}--\S\ref{sec:grand-synthesis-k3xe}):
  \begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(K3-\arabic*)}]
  \item $\kappa(K3 \times E) = 3 = \dim_\bC$, verified by
    $6$ independent paths (Proposition~\ref{prop:kappa-k3},
    Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow-k3e}; AP48).
  \item The factor~$2$ in $Z_{K3} = 2\,\phi_{0,1}$ is
    $\kappa(\cA_{K3})$; the bar complex provides the
    universal moonshine multiplier $A_n = \kappa \cdot
    \dim(\rho_n)$
    (Remark~\ref{rem:factor-2-is-kappa}).
  \item $\kappa_{\mathrm{BPS}} = \kappa(K3) + \kappa(K3 \times E)
    = 2 + 3 = 5$; ratio
    $\kappa_{\mathrm{BPS}}/\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}} = 5/3
    = \operatorname{wt}(\Phi_{10})/(2\,\dim_\bC)$;
    Hilbert--Chow exceptional $= \chi(K3) = 24$
    (Proposition~\ref{prop:kappa-bps-decomposition}).
  \item Shadow $\neq \Phi_{10}$: four structural obstructions
    O1--O4 (Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-siegel-gap}).
  \item $D^b(K3 \times E)$ constructively reconstructible
    via \v{C}ech descent ($2$ charts), BKR at Kummer,
    and Brauer vanishing
    (Remark~\ref{rem:db-k3xe-reconstruction}).
  \item Mock modular decomposition
    $Z_{K3} = (h - 24\mu)\,\vartheta_1^2/\eta^3$,
    machine-precision verified
    (Remark~\ref{rem:mock-modular-k3}).
  \item Schottky kills shadow--Siegel at $g \geq 4$,
    $\operatorname{codim} = (g{-}2)(g{-}3)/2$
    (O4 of Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-siegel-gap}).
  \item $Z^{\mathrm{sh}}$ converges with radius $2\pi$,
    Borel entire, no resurgence
    (Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow-gf-convergence}).
  \item Boundary $A_E$ ($\kappa = 24$) vs sigma $V_{K3}$
    ($\kappa = 2$): ratio $12$ at genus~$1$; conditional
    at $g \geq 2$ ($V_{K3}$ is multi-weight, AP32)
    (Proposition~\ref{prop:boundary-sigma-ratio});
    Leech connection through $q^1$
    (Remark~\ref{rem:leech-connection}).
  \item $\lambda_5^{\mathrm{FP}} = 73/3503554560$
    (AP3-corrected; the unreduced numerator
    $2^{2g-1}-1 = 511$ requires GCD reduction with
    $(2g)!$).
  \end{enumerate}

  Ten forward-looking research programmes (A--J) are
  developed in the toroidal and elliptic algebras chapter
  (Vol~III, Chapter~\ref{chap:toroidal-elliptic}), each with
  formal conjectures:
  \begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(Prog \Alph*)}]
  \item Constructive CY gluing
    (Open Problem~\ref{op:programme-a-cy-gluing},
    Conjecture~\ref{conj:ade-chart-k3}).
  \item $\kappa$ as universal moonshine multiplier
    (Open Problem~\ref{op:programme-b-moonshine},
    Conjecture~\ref{conj:universal-moonshine-multiplier}).
  \item Second-quantization bridge
    (Open Problem~\ref{op:programme-c-second-quantization},
    Conjecture~\ref{conj:kappa-bps-universality}).
  \item Schottky shadow programme
    (Open Problem~\ref{op:programme-d-schottky},
    Conjecture~\ref{conj:shadow-taut-projection}).
  \item Mock modularity and the bar complex
    (Open Problem~\ref{op:programme-e-mock-modularity},
    Conjecture~\ref{conj:mock-shadow-tower}).
  \item Modular factorization envelope
    (Open Problem~\ref{op:programme-f-factorization-envelope},
    Conjecture~\ref{conj:modular-fact-envelope}).
  \item BKM algebras and scattering diagrams
    (Open Problem~\ref{op:programme-g-bkm-scattering},
    Conjecture~\ref{conj:scattering-tropical-shadow}).
  \item Descent theorem programme
    (Open Problem~\ref{op:programme-h-descent}).
  \item Higher-dimensional CY shadows
    (Open Problem~\ref{op:programme-i-higher-dim},
    Conjecture~\ref{conj:cy-product-shadow}).
  \item Convergence vs divergence
    (Open Problem~\ref{op:programme-j-convergence}).
  \end{enumerate}
  All conjectures have status \ClaimStatusConjectured{};
  all are grounded in the $42$ CY compute engines and
  are falsifiable by explicit computation.
  \end{enumerate}

  Three additional structural results from the CY sweep:
  (K3-11)~Class~G exactness: for the free-field boundary algebra $A_E$,
    $F_g^{\mathrm{sh}} = F_g^{\mathrm{top}}$ at all genera
    (Proposition~\ref{prop:class-g-no-instantons}); no worldsheet
    instanton corrections for class-G (shadow depth~$2$) algebras.
  (K3-12)~Bar/hocolim commutation:
    $B(\operatorname{hocolim}_\sigma A_\sigma) \simeq
    \operatorname{hocolim}_\sigma B(A_\sigma)$
    (Proposition~\ref{prop:bar-hocolim}), a descent theorem for bar
    complexes; the bar functor is left Quillen, hence preserves
    homotopy colimits ($145$ tests).
  (K3-13)~$\kappa$-spectrum polysemy:
    $\operatorname{Spec}_\kappa(K3 \times E)
    = \{2, 3, 5, 24, \ldots\}$, with each value arising from a
    distinct algebraization (Remark~\ref{rem:kappa-spectrum-k3xe}).

\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Open-sector and globalisation targets}

\begin{enumerate}[resume, label=\textup{(\arabic*)}]

\item \textbf{Loop--Connes bridge}
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:vol2-loop-connes-bridge}).

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Original statement.}
  Closed genus creation (the genus-loop operator $\Lambda_P$)
  is the image of the open BV/Connes operator under the
  derived-center map.

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ reformulation.}
  The clutching sector of $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$
  has a non-separating component
  $\hbar\Delta_{\mathrm{ns}}(\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA)$
  that raises genus by one.  The derived-center map
  $\beta_{\mathrm{der}} \colon
  Z^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA) \to
  \mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{oc}}$
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:thqg-swiss-cheese}) identifies the bulk with
  a subalgebra of the open-closed convolution algebra.  The
  conjecture asserts:
  \begin{quote}
  \emph{$\beta_{\mathrm{der}}^*
  (\Delta_{\mathrm{open}}) = \Lambda_P$: the non-separating
  clutching operator
  $\Delta_{\mathrm{ns}}$ in the closed sector of
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ equals the image of the
  open-sector Connes operator $B$ under the derived-center map.}
  \end{quote}
  In words: the genus-raising mechanism in the closed sector is
  the trace mechanism in the open sector, viewed through the
  universal bulk.

\item \textbf{Global open sector on tangential log curves}
  (ledger: \textsc{Red}).

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Original statement.}
  Extend the local open/closed realization to global
  factorization on tangential log curves $(X, D, \tau)$.

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ reformulation.}
  The local-global bridge
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:thqg-local-global-bridge}) identifies the
  formal-disk restriction of the bordered FM convolution with
  $C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA, \cA)$.  The global extension
  asks for a sheaf of open-closed convolution algebras
  $\mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{oc}}_{X, D, \tau}$
  on $(X, D, \tau)$ with a global MC element
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}, \mathrm{glob}}_\cA$ whose stalk at
  each formal disk reproduces the local $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$.
  In $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ terms:
  \begin{quote}
  \emph{Does $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ glue to a global
  section of the sheaf of open-closed MC moduli on $(X, D, \tau)$,
  satisfying excision and descent for the open factorization
  category?}
  \end{quote}
  The local data are proved.  The globalisation requires
  constructing the excision sequence for the bordered FM
  compactification on curves with real-blowup boundary data.

\item \textbf{Modular periodicity for admissible simple quotients}
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:modular-periodicity-minimal}).

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{Original statement.}
  The bar cohomology dimensions of the simple quotient $L_k(\fg)$
  at admissible level are eventually periodic.

  \smallskip\noindent
  \emph{$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ reformulation.}
  The conjectured periodic CDG structure
  asserts $2p$-periodicity of
  the bar complex of $L_k(\fg)$.  In
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ terms, this periodicity should be
  visible as a $\mathbb{Z}/2p\mathbb{Z}$-grading on the
  open-closed convolution algebra
  $\mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{oc}}_{L_k}$ inherited from the
  cyclotomic chart:
  \begin{quote}
  \emph{Does the $\mu_q$-grading of the cyclotomic boundary chart
  induce an eventual periodicity on the graded pieces of
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_{L_k}$?}
  \end{quote}
  The proved closed-sector input: T-matrix periodicity (Step~1)
  and bar differential lift (Step~3).  The open gap: the
  convolution with $1/\eta$ (Step~2) may break eventual
  periodicity of Fourier coefficients.

\end{enumerate}

\begin{remark}[The $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ meta-principle]
\label{rem:theta-oc-meta-principle}
\index{Theta-oc@$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$!meta-principle}
Every open problem in this monograph is a question about
a specific projection, extension, or structural property of
$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$.  The proved core establishes
existence of $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ and its MC equation
at all genera.  The open problems fall into three classes:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \emph{Identification problems}: which tautological class
  does a given projection produce?
  (Multi-generator universality, Pixton generation, arithmetic
  comparison.)  These require computing specific coefficients
  of $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$.
\item \emph{Extension problems}: does $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$
  extend to a larger domain (analytic completion, global curves,
  coderived categories, module categories)?
  (Analytic realization, boundary bar duality, categorical KD,
  globalisation, modular cooperad.)
\item \emph{Functoriality problems}: is $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$
  preserved under a given functor (DS reduction, factorization
  envelope, BV quantization)?
  (DS--KD intertwining, modular factorization adjunction, BV/BRST bridge,
  DK bridge.)
\end{enumerate}
The programme is: compute more projections~(a), prove more
extensions~(b), establish more functorialities~(c).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Five open problems as questions about
$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$]
\label{rem:five-problems-theta-oc}
\index{open problems!five key reformulations}
The preceding section develops each reformulation in detail.
The following digest records the essential question in each case.

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{Multi-generator universality}
  \textup{(}Open Problem~\ref{op:multi-generator-universality},
  \textbf{resolved negatively}\textup{)}.
  The closed projection
  $\pi_{\mathrm{cl}}(\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA)|_g$
  is $\kappa(\cA) \cdot \lambda_g$ on the uniform-weight lane.
  For multi-weight algebras at $g \geq 2$, the scalar formula
  fails: $F_g(\cA) = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}} +
  \delta F_g^{\mathrm{cross}}(\cA)$ with
  $\delta F_g^{\mathrm{cross}} \neq 0$
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:multi-weight-genus-expansion}).
  The clutching sector does NOT force
  $\Gamma_\cA = \kappa(\cA)\Lambda$; the Kuranishi map
  vanishes by parity.

\item \emph{BV/BRST $=$ bar at higher genus}
  \textup{(}Conjecture~\ref{conj:master-bv-brst}\textup{)}.
  The BV path integral on $\Sigma_g$ produces
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{BV}}_T
  \in \MC(\mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{BV}}_T)$.
  At genus~$0$, the PVA descent theorems identify the two
  convolution algebras and their MC elements.
  The question: does the identification
  $\mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA|_{g \geq 1}
  \simeq \mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{BV}}_T|_{g \geq 1}$
  hold, sending $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ to
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{BV}}_T$?

\item \emph{Pixton ideal generation}
  \textup{(}Conjecture~\ref{conj:pixton-from-shadows}\textup{)}.
  For class-M algebras, each genus-$g$ component of the MC equation
  $D\Theta_\cA + \tfrac{1}{2}[\Theta_\cA,\Theta_\cA]
  + \hbar\Delta(\Theta_\cA) = 0$
  projects to a tautological relation in
  $R^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)$.
  The question: does the ideal generated by
  $\{\operatorname{taut}_{g,n}([\Theta_\cA]_{g,n}) :
  g,n \geq 0,\; \cA \in \text{class M}\}$
  equal the Pixton ideal?

\item \emph{Arithmetic comparison}
  \textup{(}Conjecture~\ref{conj:arithmetic-comparison}\textup{)}.
  The genus-$1$ shadow $\pi_{\mathrm{cl}}(\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA)|_1$
  determines the shadow spectral measure and hence the arithmetic
  packet connection $\nabla^{\mathrm{arith}}_\cA$.
  The question: do the higher-genus components
  $\pi_{\mathrm{cl}}(\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA)|_{g \geq 2}$
  determine the residues of the frontier defect form $\Omega_\cA$
  at scattering poles?

\item \emph{Analytic realization}
  \textup{(}Conjecture~\ref{conj:analytic-realization}\textup{)}.
  The algebraic MC element $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ lives in the
  formal convolution algebra.  The question: does the inclusion
  $\mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA \hookrightarrow
  \hat{\mathfrak{g}}{}^{\mathrm{oc},\mathrm{an}}_\cA$
  into an analytic completion send $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ to a
  completed MC element
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc},\mathrm{an}}_\cA$
  whose genus-$g$ amplitudes converge via trace-class sewing?
  Proved for Heisenberg and lattice VOAs; open in general.
\end{enumerate}
Items~(i) and~(iii) are identification problems: which cohomology
class does a given projection of $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ produce?
Item~(ii) is a functoriality problem: is $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$
the image of $\Theta^{\mathrm{BV}}_T$ under a comparison functor?
Items~(iv) and~(v) are extension problems: does the MC element
carry information beyond the formal/algebraic setting?
\end{remark}

% ======================================================================
\section{Forbidden slogans}
\label{sec:concordance-forbidden-slogans}
\index{forbidden slogans}
% ======================================================================

The following statements are false.
They must never appear in this monograph.
Each violates a specific anti-pattern documented
in the Beilinson Principle
(\S\ref{sec:concordance-conjecture-promotions}).

\begin{enumerate}

\item \textbf{``Bar $=$ bulk.''}
  \emph{False.}
  The bar complex $\barB(\cA)$ classifies
  \emph{twisting morphisms}:
  algebraic maps $\tau \colon \barB(\cA) \to \cA$
  controlling the coupling between~$\cA$ and its
  Koszul dual~$\cA^!$.
  The bulk algebra is the
  \emph{chiral derived center}
  $Z^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)
  = H^*(C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA, \cA), \delta)$,
  which classifies bulk operators acting on the
  boundary
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:thqg-swiss-cheese}).
  These are different objects produced by different
  functors.
  \emph{Violated anti-pattern}: AP25
  (three functors, three outputs:
  bar~$\neq$ Verdier dual~$\neq$ cobar).

\item \textbf{``The boundary algebra is the
  primitive object.''}
  \emph{False.}
  The primitive object is the open-sector
  factorization dg-category
  $\mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{op}}$ on a tangential log
  curve $(X, D, \tau)$ with real-oriented blowup at
  each puncture, not on the ordinary curve~$X$.
  The boundary algebra
  $A_b = \mathrm{End}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{op}}}(b)$
  is an endomorphism algebra of a chosen
  boundary condition~$b$: a Morita-dependent chart,
  not the intrinsic datum.
  Different choices of~$b$ produce Morita-equivalent
  but non-isomorphic algebras.
  \emph{Violated anti-pattern}: AP9
  (same name, different object: the chart is not
  the category).

\item \textbf{``All master conjectures resolved.''}
  \emph{Misleading.}
  All five MC1--MC5 are proved: MC3 is proved for all
  simple types on the evaluation-generated core
  (Corollary~\ref{cor:mc3-all-types}).  But
  the broader programme contains open problems downstream
  of MC3: the DK-4/5 extension/completion packet
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk-compacts-completion}),
  multi-generator universality at $g \geq 2$
  (Open Problem~\ref{op:multi-generator-universality}, now
  resolved negatively: cross-channel correction nonzero),
  modular cooperad completion,
  D-module purity converse,
  Pixton ideal generation
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:pixton-from-shadows}),
  and the arithmetic comparison conjecture.
  The five MC statements are proved; the programme
  continues beyond them.
  \emph{Violated anti-pattern}: AP7
  (scope inflation: universal claim obscuring downstream residuals).

\item \textbf{``Gravity Yangian at strict level.''}
  \emph{False.}
  The Virasoro dg-shifted Yangian is a
  \emph{cohomological} object: it is a dg Lie
  algebra with a transferred $L_\infty$ structure
  from the DS reduction
  (Vol~II, Theorem~\textup{thm:ds-hpl-transfer}).
  It is not a strict Yangian in the sense of
  Drinfeld: the higher operations
  $\ell_k$ for $k \geq 3$ are nonzero
  (Virasoro has shadow depth $r_{\max} = \infty$,
  class~M).
  Writing ``strict'' erases the entire
  non-formality content of the shadow obstruction tower.
  \emph{Violated anti-pattern}: AP14
  (conflating Koszulness with formality:
  Virasoro is Koszul but not $\mathrm{SC}$-formal).

\item \textbf{``The modular cooperad package is proved.''}
  \emph{False.}
  The modular cooperad structure on
  $\mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{op}}$ is a
  \emph{programme}, not a theorem.
  Stage~4 of the four-stage open/closed architecture
  (trace $+$ clutching on the open sector)
  has the annulus trace proved
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:thqg-annulus-trace}),
  but the full modular cooperad (all genera,
  all boundary conditions, full sewing compatibility)
  is not constructed.
  \emph{Violated anti-pattern}: AP7
  (scope inflation: programme described as proved).

\item \textbf{``$\Theta_\cA + \Theta_{\cA^!} = 0$
  at full level.''}
  \emph{False.}
  Only the scalar projection is constrained:
  $\kappa(\cA) + \kappa(\cA^!) = 0$
  for Kac--Moody and free-field families,
  and $\kappa(\cA) + \kappa(\cA^!) = \rho \cdot K$
  for $\Walg$-algebras
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:genus-universality}).
  The full MC elements $\Theta_\cA$ and
  $\Theta_{\cA^!}$ are related by the
  Verdier involution on $\Ran(X)$
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-isomorphism-main}),
  but this involution is \emph{not} negation:
  it intertwines bar and cobar, sending
  $\barB(\cA)$ to $\barB(\cA^!)$, not to
  $-\barB(\cA)$.
  The higher-arity shadows
  (cubic~$C$, quartic~$Q$, etc.)
  satisfy independent complementarity relations
  that are not simple sign changes.
  \emph{Violated anti-patterns}: AP24
  ($\kappa + \kappa^! = 0$ overclaimed;
  for Virasoro, $\kappa + \kappa^! = 13$)
  and AP31
  ($\kappa = 0$ does not imply $\Theta = 0$:
  scalar vanishing does not force full-tower
  vanishing).

\item \textbf{``Virasoro is not Koszul.''}
  \emph{False.}
  Virasoro is chirally Koszul: the bar cohomology
  $H^*(\barB(\mathrm{Vir}_c))$ is concentrated
  in bar degree~$1$ for generic~$c$
  (Corollary~\ref{cor:universal-koszul},
  via Proposition~\ref{prop:pbw-universality}).
  What Virasoro is \emph{not} is Swiss-cheese formal:
  the higher Swiss-cheese operations
  $m_k^{\mathrm{SC}} \neq 0$ for $k \geq 3$
  (shadow depth $r_{\max} = \infty$, class~M).
  Koszulness (bar concentration) and formality
  (vanishing of higher operations) are
  different properties of different objects.
  \emph{Violated anti-pattern}: AP14
  (conflating chiral Koszulness with
  Swiss-cheese formality).

\item \textbf{``The global open sector lives on an
  ordinary curve.''}
  \emph{False.}
  The open-sector factorization dg-category
  $\mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{op}}$ lives on a tangential
  log curve $(X, D, \tau)$ with real-oriented blowup
  at each puncture
  (Volume~II, Definition~\textup{def:bordified-curve}),
  not on the ordinary curve~$X$.  The boundary
  intervals $I_{p_i} = S^1_{p_i} \setminus
  \{\tau_{p_i}\} \cong \R$ carry the topological
  ($E_1$) structure; the interior carries the
  holomorphic (chiral) structure.  Omitting the
  tangential data loses the $E_1$-direction entirely.

\item \textbf{``Modularity is a property of the closed
  algebra alone.''}
  \emph{False.}
  Modularity arises from trace and clutching on the
  open sector.  The annulus trace
  $\int_{S^1} \mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{op}} \simeq
  HH_*(\cA)$ is the first modular shadow
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:thqg-annulus-trace});
  clutching along shared boundary circles raises
  genus.  The scalar $\kappa(\cA)$ enters as the trace
  of the cyclic pairing on~$\End(b)$, not as
  primitive closed-string data.  The MC equation on
  the bordered FM compactification packages both
  sectors; the closed projection is
  $F_g = \kappa \int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g}
  \lambda_g$.

\item \textbf{``The dg-shifted Yangian is a universal
  theorem for general 3d HT QFT.''}
  \emph{False.}
  On the affine lineage, the open-colour Koszul dual
  is a dg-shifted Yangian
  (Vol~II, Theorem~\textup{thm:Koszul\_dual\_Yangian}:
  \emph{proved}).
  On the chirally Koszul locus, the Yangian
  recognition theorem
  (Vol~II, Theorem~\textup{thm:yangian-recognition}) identifies
  the $\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$-algebra
  structure on~$\cA^!_{\mathrm{line}}$ with the
  dg-shifted Yangian package: \emph{proved
  algebraically}.  For general perturbative 3d HT
  theories beyond the affine lineage, the
  gravitational-Yangian package is
  \emph{conjectural}
  (Dimofte--Niu--Py~\cite{DNP25}).

\item \textbf{``Bosonization is Koszul duality.''}
  \emph{False.}
  Bosonization ($\psi \otimes \psi \cong \cH_1$
  on the $\mathbb{Z}$-lattice) is a complex-fermion to
  compactified-boson equivalence preserving~$c = 1$.
  Koszul duality ($\psi \mapsto
  \mathrm{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\gamma)$)
  maps a real fermion at $c = 1/2$ to a boson at
  $c = -1/2$, reversing sign.  These are different
  functors on different objects with different outputs
  (Remark~\ref{rem:bosonization-not-koszul}).
  \emph{Violated anti-pattern}: AP25
  (confusing two operations that share a surface
  resemblance).

\end{enumerate}
